    呃门

    　　　　黄帝素问

    　　　　　至真要大论

    　　少阴之复，燠热内作，外为浮肿哕噫。　　【注　哕者，小肠之气不通。逆气上走心而为噫也。】　　阳明之复，清气大举，甚则心痛否满，腹胀而泄，呕苦咳哕，烦心，病在鬲中。　　 【注　咳哕，肺气逆也。咳哕烦心者，病在鬲中，阳明之气上逆也。】　　太阳之复，厥气上行，唾出清水及为哕噫。　　 【注　唾出清水及为哕噫，从胃而上及于心也。】
    　　　　灵枢经

    　　　　　邪气脏腑病形篇[1p]

    Collection of Medical Works from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 325

    Eyelid Disorders

    Huangdi’s Suwen

    Discussion on the Essential Truths

    When the Young Yin recovers, internal heat results, leading to external swelling and belching. (Note: Belching refers to the irregular flow of Qi in the small intestine, ascending to the heart and resulting in belching.) When the Yangming recovers, clear Qi rises strongly; in severe cases, there may be heart pain, fullness in the abdomen, diarrhea, bitter vomiting, cough and belching, restlessness, and the disease is in the diaphragm. (Note: Coughing and belching indicate reversed lung Qi; coughing and restlessness signify the disease is in the diaphragm, and the Yangming Qi is ascending abnormally.) When the Taiyang recovers, there is an ascent of deficiency Qi, leading to the spitting of clear water and belching. (Note: Spitting clear water and belching indicates movement from the stomach upward to the heart.)

    Lingshu Sutra

    On the Symptoms of Diseases in the Internal Organs[1p]

    　　心脉小甚为善哕。
    　　 【注　心脏虚而火土之气弱也。】
    　　　　　九针论

    　　胃为气逆哕。
    　　 【注　有故寒气与新谷气，俱还入于胃，新故相乱，真邪相攻，气并相逆，复出于胃，故为哕。】
    　　　　　杂病篇

    　　哕，以草刺鼻嚏，嚏而已；无息而疾迎引之，立已；大惊之亦可已。　　 【注　阳明所受谷气，欲从肺而达表，肺气逆还于胃，气并相逆，复出于胃，故为哕。以草刺鼻，取嚏以通肺，肺气疏通，则谷气得以转输而呃逆止矣。鼻气不通而无息，则疾迎引之，连取其嚏也。大惊则肝心之气分散，胃之逆气，亦可从之而外达也。】
    　　　　金匮要略 【汉　张机】

    　　　　　哕病证治

    　　黄疸病小便色不变，欲自利，腹满而喘，不可除热，热除必哕。哕者，小半夏汤主之。　　《千金翼》小承气汤，治大便不通，哕数讝语。　　哕而腹满，视其前后，知何部不利，利之即愈。
    　　　　中藏经 【汉　华佗】[2p]

    The heart pulse is very weak and prone to hiccups.
    [Note: This refers to the heart being deficient and the energies of fire and earth being weak.]
    — Discussion on Nine Needles

    The stomach experiences reversed qi, resulting in hiccups.
    [Note: This indicates that both cold air and new grain qi have entered the stomach, creating confusion between the old and the new, with true and false forces clashing, causing reversed qi that subsequently emerges from the stomach, hence the hiccups.]
    — Treatise on Miscellaneous Diseases

    Hiccups can occur from nasal irritation due to herbs, causing sneezing, which serves only to expel the air; if there is no breathing and it happens quickly, it can be resolved immediately; severe fright can also help.
    [Note: The grain qi received by the Yangming channel desires to reach the surface via the lungs, but the lung qi returns to the stomach, causing reversed qi that comes out of the stomach, leading to hiccups. Nasal irritation can induce sneezing to open the lungs; when lung qi is unobstructed, the grain qi can be properly transported, stopping the hiccups. If nasal qi is obstructed and there is no breathing, prompt sneezing is necessary. Severe fright can scatter the qi of the liver and heart, allowing reversed stomach qi to exit.]
    — Essential Prescriptions of the Golden Coffer

    Hiccup-related ailments and treatments:
    In cases of jaundice with unchanged urine color, the desire to pass stool, fullness in the abdomen and breathlessness, one should not eliminate heat; if heat is removed, hiccups will occur. For hiccups, Xiao Banxia Decoction is prescribed.
    — Prescription for One Thousands Gold
    Xiao Chengqi Decoction is for treating constipation and multiple hiccups.
    If hiccups are accompanied by abdominal fullness, examining preceding and following symptoms indicates which area is obstructed; addressing that will lead to recovery.
    — Classic of Internal Medicine [2p]

    　　　　　脾病

    　　脾胀则喜哕，四肢急，体重不食，善噫。　　寒则阴中与腰脊俱疼，面黑耳干，哕不能食，或呕血是也。
    　　　　活人书 【宋　朱肱】

    　　　　　伤寒证

    　　咳逆者，仲景所谓哕者是也。哕，胃寒所生。伤寒本虚，攻其热必哕。又云：伤寒大吐下之极虚，复发汗者，其人水气怫郁，复与之水，以发其汗，因得哕。所以然者，胃中寒故也，橘皮干姜汤、羌活附子散、半夏生姜汤、退阴散主之。若服药不瘥者，灸之必愈。其法：妇人屈乳头向下尽处骨间，灸三壮；丈夫及乳小者，以一指为率。正以男左女右，艾炷如小豆许，与乳相直间陷中动脉处是。然亦有阳证咳逆者，小柴胡汤、橘皮竹茹汤。仲景又云：伤寒哕而腹满，视其前后，知何部不利，利之即愈。仲景无方。前部宜猪苓汤，后部宜调胃承气汤。扁鹊《中藏经》治伤寒咳逆，丁香散。丁香、柿蒂各一分，甘草、良姜各半钱，沸汤点作一服，乘热猛吃，极效。[3p]

    Spleen Disease

    If the spleen is distended, there will be joy in belching, with urgency in the limbs, a heavy body, and a tendency to sigh. In cold conditions, there will be pain in the lower back and spine, a dark face with dry ears, inability to eat due to belching, or possibly vomiting blood.

    Febrile Disease Symptoms

    A reverse cough is what Zhang Zhongjing referred to as belching. Belching arises from cold in the stomach. Febrile disease is fundamentally deficient; attacking its heat must lead to belching. Moreover, it is said that if a febrile disease leads to extreme vomiting and diarrhea, and sweating is induced again, the person will have water stagnating, and if water is given to bring forth sweat, belching will occur. This is due to the coldness in the stomach. The treatment involves using dried tangerine peel and ginger decoction, or a formula of Qiang Huo and Fu Zi, or a decoction of Ban Xia and ginger, or the Tui Yin San. If taking medicine does not heal, moxibustion will surely cure. The method: for women, bend the nipple down towards the bone in between, and moxibustion three times; for men and small-breasted individuals, take one finger as a measure. Position is important: men on the left, women on the right, burning moxa the size of a small bean directly above the pulsing artery midpoint. However, there are also those with a yang syndrome experiencing a reverse cough, treated with Xiao Chai Hu Tang or tangerine peel and bamboo leaf decoction. Zhang Zhongjing also says: if belching occurs with abdominal fullness, by examining the front and back, one can discern which part is obstructed, and relieving that will lead to recovery. Zhang Zhongjing offers no specific formula. The front should use Zhu Ling Decoction, and the back should use Tiao Wei Cheng Qi Decoction. Bian Que's "Zhong Cang Jing" recommends for febrile cough and reverse cough, using the Clove Powder. Mix cloves and persimmon calyx each at one part, and licorice and ginger each at half a part; boil in hot water to form a dose, and consume it while hot for utmost efficacy.[3p]

    　　《三因》第十一卷又有竹茹汤等方，亦丁香散方。竹茹汤治阳证也。　　《本事方》第八卷，治伤寒候，咳逆豆蔻汤。治阴证咳逆，丁香、茴香、肉豆蔻等药。若阳证不可用。　　凡咳逆多有先热而吃生冷，或凉药多，相激而成，盖阴阳二气相搏。邻人之仆，本发大热，以凉药下之，想太甚，咳逆四五日，竟至于服丁香柿蒂而后，却再以小柴胡之属解其余热，遂愈。下后盖有身热不解也。　　治伤寒咳逆，后二方出抚州华盖山周先生，惟一备急方救急方，香附子、橘核各半两，细銼，用酒半盏，先将药在石银器内炒，渐渐滴酒炒药焦黄色，研细末，每二钱，水一小盏，煎至八分，细细旋呷服。一方单用香附子末，一方用大蒜头二个，煨动爆研，入白姜末，丸得为度，丸如梧桐子大，捣薤菜自然汁，吞下二十圆。病退，再服一十五圆。[4p]

    In Volume 11 of "San Yin," there are also prescriptions such as Bamboo Rhizome Decoction and Clove Powder. Bamboo Rhizome Decoction treats Yang syndromes.

    In Volume 8 of "Ben Shi Fang," for treating the symptoms of cold damage, there is a prescription for cough and counterflow with Cardamom Decoction. For treating Yin syndrome's cough and counterflow, medications like Clove, Fennel, and Nutmeg are used, while they are unsuitable for Yang syndromes.

    Coughing and counterflow often arise from initial heat followed by the intake of raw and cold substances or too many cooling medications, leading to conflicting Qi between Yin and Yang. A neighboring servant had a strong fever, and after using cooling medications excessively, experienced coughing and counterflow for four to five days. Eventually, only after taking Clove and Persimmon stem did they improve. Following that, they used Xiao Chai Hu for lingering heat and recovered afterwards, indicating that the fever was not fully resolved.

    For treating cold damage with cough and counterflow, two prescriptions were subsequently provided by Mr. Zhou from Huagai Mountain in Fuzhou. One is an emergency prescription: half a tael of Cyperus tuber and tangerine seed, finely shredded, fried together in half a cup of wine until the medicine turns a golden yellow, ground into a fine powder. Take two qian with a small cup of water, decoct it until down to eight parts, and sip it slowly.

    One formula uses only the powder of Cyperus, while another incorporates two cloves of garlic, sautéed and ground, mixed with white ginger powder, formed into pills the size of the seeds of the Wutong tree, and swallowed with the juice of Shao Cai in a dose of twenty pills. When the illness recedes, take another fifteen pills.[4p]

    　　　　济生方 【宋　严用和】

    　　　　　论证

    　　夫咳逆之病，详考诸书，无该载者。唯孙真人云：咳逆遍寻方论，无此名称，但古人以咳逆为哕耳。多因吐利之后，胃中虚寒，遂成此证。亦有胃气鬲上热，哕至八九声相连，收气不回者，却当子细看脉与证，施以治法。大抵老人、虚人、久病人及妇人产后有此证者，皆是病深之候，非佳兆也。[5p]

    Ji Sheng Fang
    (Song Dynasty - Yan Yonghe)

    Discussion

    The disease of coughing and reverse flow, upon careful examination of various texts, is not explicitly recorded. Only Master Sun mentions that there is no specific term for "coughing and reverse flow" in the discussions of herbal formulas, but that the ancients referred to it as "coughing and reverse sounds." This often occurs after vomiting or purging, leading to a condition of emptiness and cold in the stomach, which gives rise to this symptom. There are also cases where stomach qi ascends with heat, resulting in coughing with eight or nine continuous sounds, where breath is unable to return. In such cases, one should carefully examine the pulse and symptoms and apply appropriate treatments. Generally, this condition is observed in the elderly, the weak, those suffering from prolonged illnesses, and women after childbirth. These are all signs of a deep-seated illness, not favorable omens.[5p]

    　　　　明理论 【金　成无己】

    　　　　　伤寒证治

    　　伤寒哕者，何以明之？哕者，俗谓之咳逆，吃吃然有声者是也。若[食(句去口改吉)]则但胸喉间气噎塞不得下通，然而无声也，皆胃之疾，但轻重有差尔。虚寒相搏，反饮水令汗大出，水得寒气，冷必相搏，其人即[食(句去口改吉)]，言胃气虚竭也。伤寒大吐大下之后极虚，复发汗出者，其人外气怫郁，复与之水，以发其汗，因得哕，所以然者，胃中寒冷故也。又胃中虚冷不能食者，饮水则哕，由是皆胃疾可知矣。经曰：趺阳脉浮则为虚，关脉滑则为哕，此为医咎，责虚取实之过也。大抵妄下之后，胃中气逆，则成哕也。[6p]

    The Theory of Ming
    (Jin Cheng Wujǐ)

    On the Treatment of Febrile Diseases

    How can one clarify the signs of a febrile disease characterized by eructation? Eructation is commonly referred to as a reverse cough, which is characterized by a sound of gulping. If food obstructs the chest and throat, causing the qi to become blocked and unable to descend, there is no sound; this is purely a gastric disorder, albeit with varying degrees of severity. When there is a clash of vacuous cold and one drinks cold water, it induces a large sweating response; the cold qi clashes with the body, leading to eructation after consuming food, indicative of the depletion of gastric qi. After excessive vomiting and purging in cases of severe vacuity, if sweating recurs, it suggests the external qi is stagnant. If one then consumes water to induce sweating, it leads to eructation, which is due to the coldness in the stomach. Furthermore, if the stomach is vacuous and cold, making it unable to receive food, drinking water will also trigger eructation, indicating various gastric disorders. The classics mention: "If the Fuyang pulse is floating, it indicates vacuity; if the Guan pulse is slippery, it indicates eructation." This suggests a medical fault, blaming the state of vacuity for the real issues at hand. In general, after excessive purging, if the qi in the stomach is reversed, it ultimately leads to eructation.[6p]

    经曰：湿家若下之太早则哕；胃中本虚，攻其热则哕；而阳明病不能食，攻其热必哕。诸如此者，皆下之后胃虚而然也。然[食(句去口改吉)]者正为水寒相搏，必用小青龙汤去麻黄加附子而可矣。至于哕者，则又热气壅郁，气不得通而戊者也。轻者有和解之证，重者有攻下之候。经曰：有潮热时时哕，与小柴胡汤，即是和解之证也。哕而腹满，视其前后，知何部不利，利之则愈，即是攻下之候也。伤寒至于哕，则病已极矣，非若渴烦等轻缓之候。如太阳中风，以火劫发汗，阴阳俱虚竭，身体枯燥，但头汗出，剂颈而还，腹满微喘，口干咽烂，或不大便，久则讝语，甚者至哕，是言其极也。又不尿腹满加哕者不治，是为真病。其若是者，虽有神术，当斯脱绝之候，又何以措其手足哉？[7p]

    The classics state: If one purges a phlegmatic patient too early, it will cause vomiting; if the stomach is originally weak and one attacks its heat, it will cause vomiting; and in cases of Yangming disease where one cannot eat, attacking the heat will surely cause vomiting. All of these situations occur due to the stomach being weak after purging. However, burping is primarily due to the cold water clashing against the stomach, thus one must use Minor Blue Dragon Decoction, removing Ephedra and adding Aconite. As for burping, it is also caused by the obstruction of heat, where qi cannot flow properly. If mild, it indicates a need for harmonization; if severe, it indicates a need for purging. The classics state: When there are tidal fevers accompanied by burping, correlating with Minor Chaihu Decoction, this is a sign of harmonization. If there is burping along with abdominal fullness, by examining conditions before and after, one can understand which part is obstructed; relieving it will lead to recovery, which points to the need for purging. When a cold damage leads to burping, the illness has reached an extreme, unlike lighter conditions such as thirst or irritation. In cases of Sun Pattern Wind, where fire harms and causes sweating, both yin and yang are completely exhausted, leaving the body dry, with only head sweat coming, slightly returning to the neck, abdominal fullness, mild wheezing, dry mouth, and throat decay, and possibly no bowel movements—if prolonged, it leads to disorientation, and in severe cases to burping, indicating an extreme condition. Furthermore, if there is no urination along with abdominal fullness and burping, this condition cannot be treated and represents a true illness. In such cases, although there are divine methods, it’s a situation where one may be helpless; how could one possibly respond?[7p]

    　　　　东垣十书 【元　李杲】

    　　　　　辨证别名

    　　咳逆，俗以呃逆与呃忒呼之。然咳逆二字，仅见《伤寒论》首辨脉平脉法中，其六经病篇及汗下可否诸篇皆无所有。后人因见六经病篇及汗下可否诸篇，但有哕而无咳逆，遂谓曰咳逆。吁！斯言也，孙真人倡于前，朱奉议、成无己和于后，由是二者之名义紊矣。《金匮要略》曰：病人胸中似喘不喘，似呕不呕，似哕不哕，彻心中愦愦然无奈者，生姜半夏汤主之。干呕，哕，若手足厥者，橘皮汤主之。哕逆者，橘皮竹茹汤主之。观此，则仲景但指与干呕同类者言，何尝指与咳逆言乎？咳逆言其声之才发而遽止，虽发止相续，有至数十声者，然而短促不长，有若咳嗽之咳然。故曰咳逆哕逆，则言其似欲呕物以出而无所出，但声之浊恶，长而有力，直至气尽而后止，非如干呕之轻而不甚，故二者皆由气之逆上而作，故俱以逆言。[8p]

    Distinguishing Symptoms and Terminology

    Cough-reversal, commonly referred to as 'a-逆' (e-reversing) or 'a-忒' (e-taste), is mentioned only in the "Treatise on Cold Damage" under the section on distinguishing the pulse. However, in the chapters on the six disorders and whether to induce sweating or purging, there is no mention of it. Later scholars, upon seeing the sections on the six disorders and whether to induce sweating or purging, noted that only 'a' is mentioned without reference to cough-reversal, thus labeling it as cough-reversal. Alas! This assertion originated from Master Sun, followed by discussions from Zhu and Cheng, which led to confusion over the definitions of the two terms. The "Essential Prescriptions from the Golden Coffer" states: If a patient appears as if they are panting without actually panting, as if they are vomiting without truly vomiting, and as if they are 'a' without being 'a', yet feels bewildered in their chest with no relief, Ginger and Pinellia Decoction is indicated. For dry retching, 'a', or if there are symptoms of limb coldness, Orange Peel Decoction is indicated. For instances of 'a' and cough-reversal, Orange Peel and Bamboo Shavings Decoction is indicated. From this, it is clear that Zhang Zhongjing only identifies it among those similar to dry retching and does not reference cough-reversal. Cough-reversal denotes a sound that abruptly starts and stops; although it may be repeated several times, it is short and quick, resembling a cough in its sound. Therefore, the mention of cough-reversal and 'a' implies a desire to expel something but with nothing being expelled, characterized by a harsh and potent sound, lasting until the breath is exhausted before ceasing, unlike the light and less intense nature of dry retching. Thus, both arise from upward-reversed qi, which is why they are both described as 'reversed'.[8p]

    《伤寒》虽以辨脉平脉法之咳逆，与咳逆上气视为呃忒，然安知其不为咳而气逆之病乎？故今不敢定其必为吃忒也。《金匮要略》曰：病咳逆，寸口脉微而数，此为肺痈。咳逆上气，时时唾浊，但坐不得眠，皂荚丸主之。咳而上气，喉中水鸡声，射干麻黄汤主之。此三条者皆是咳而气逆之病，岂可以咳逆专为呃忒哉？今伤寒家本有呃忒，而六经病篇及汗下可否诸篇却无者，必亡逸于散落之余耳。虽呃忒为六经病篇及汗下可否诸篇所不言，决不可以哕为呃忒之咳逆，亦不可以哕为咳而气逆之咳逆也。或曰：吾子以《要略》所谓哕逆非呃忒病，何后人治呃忒者，用橘皮竹茹汤而愈乎？余曰：橘皮竹茹汤，辛甘之剂也，有散有缓，有和有补，其二证虽不同，而为邪正之气怫郁扰乱所致则一，故用焉而皆愈。虽然，二证以一药同治则可，以一体同视则不可。[9p]

    Although "Shang Han" distinguishes between cough and reverse flow using the pulse method, and considers cough with reverse flow to be related to hiccups, how can we be sure this is not simply a case of cough leading to breath reversal? Therefore, I cannot assert that it must be hiccups. "Jin Kui Yao Lue" states: for illness characterized by cough and reverse flow, a thin and rapid pulse at the cun position indicates lung abscess. When cough and breath reversal occur, with frequent expectoration of turbid phlegm and an inability to lie down and sleep, use the Zao Jia Wan. If the cough causes breath reversal with a sound like waterfowl in the throat, the She Gan Ma Huang Tang should be employed. These three cases all involve cough and breath reversal; how can we solely categorize cough and reverse flow as hiccups? Currently, while practitioners of Shang Han may consider hiccups, the sections on the six meridians and whether to induce sweating or purging do not mention it, indicating it may have been neglected in the writings. Although hiccups are not discussed in the six meridians section or related sections, one cannot equate cough with breath reversal to hiccups, nor can they conflate cough and breath reversal with hiccups. Some say: you claim that the "Yao Lue" depicts reverse flow not as hiccups; why, then, do later practitioners treat hiccups using Tangerine Peel and Bamboo Shavings Decoction and achieve recoveries? I respond: Tangerine Peel and Bamboo Shavings Decoction is a formula that is spicy and sweet, having both dispersing and soothing properties, as well as harmonizing and nourishing effects. Despite the differing symptoms, the cause remains the same—an imbalance of pathogenic and righteous qi leading to turmoil. Thus, it can be effectively used for both. Nonetheless, treating two conditions with the same medicine is acceptable, but viewing them as one entity is not.[9p]

    　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　论证治

    　　呃病，呃逆也，气自脐下直冲，上出于口而作声也。《书》曰：火炎上。《内经》曰：诸逆冲上，皆属于火。东垣谓火与元气不两立。又谓火，元气之贼也。古方悉以胃弱言之，而不及火，且以丁香、柿蒂、竹茹、陈皮等剂治之，未审孰为降火，孰为补虚。人之阴气，依胃为养，胃土伤损，则木气侮之，此土败木贼也。阴为火所乘，不得内守，木挟相火乘之，故直冲清道而上。言胃弱者阴弱也，虚之甚也，病人见此似为危证。然有实者，不可不知。　　咳逆有痰、气虚、阴火，视其有余不足治之。不足者，人参白朮汤下大补丸；有余并有痰者吐之，人参芦之类。痰凝气滞而呃逆，用蜜水吐，此乃燥痰不出。[10p]

    Danxi's Heart Method
    Yuan Dynasty - Zhu Zhenheng

    Discussion on Treatment

    Belching is a reverse reaction, where the qi surges upward from below the navel and escapes through the mouth, making a sound. The Book states: "Fire rises." The Inner Canon says: "All reverse movements that surge upward belong to fire." Dongyuan argues that fire cannot coexist with the original qi, asserting that fire is a thief of the original qi. Ancient prescriptions always described this condition as a weakness of the stomach without addressing the fire, and treated it with remedies such as clove, persimmon stems, bamboo shavings, and dried citrus peel. It remains unclear which truly reduces fire and which compensates for emptiness.

    The yin qi of a person depends on the stomach for nourishment. When the stomach is damaged, the wood qi oppresses it, which is a matter of earth being defeated and wood being robbed. The yin is overrun by fire, unable to be contained internally; the wood, led by the fire, thus surges upward through the clear pathway. To say the stomach is weak means the yin is weak; if this weakness is severe, it may appear to be a critical condition. However, one must be mindful of actual deficiencies.

    For coughs with belching, weak qi, or yin fire, one should observe whether there is excess or deficiency to treat accordingly. For deficiency, use Ren Shen Bai Zhu Decoction or Major Tonifying Pill; for excess accompanied by phlegm, induce vomiting with Ren Shen and similar herbs. When phlegm has solidified and qi is stagnant, using honey water for vomiting can help; this indicates dryness of phlegm that cannot be expelled.[10p]

    　　痰者，陈皮半夏。气虚，人参、白朮。阴火，黄连、黄蘗、滑石。咳逆自痢者，滑石、甘草、炒黄蘗、白芍、人参、白朮、陈皮，加竹荆沥服。　　咳逆为病，古谓之哕，近谓之呃，乃胃寒所生，寒气由逆而上，此证最危。亦有属热者，已见伤寒证。其有他病发呃者，宜用半夏一两，生姜半两，水煎热服；或理中汤加枳壳、茯苓各半钱，半夏一钱；不效，更加丁香十粒。　　吐利后胃虚寒咳逆者，以羌活附子汤，或丁香十粒，柿蒂十个，切碎水煎服。吐利后胃热咳逆者，以竹皮竹茹汤。　　亦无别病，偶然致呃，此缘气逆而生，宜小半夏茯苓汤加枳实、半夏。又或煎汤泡萝卜子，研取汁，调木香调气散热服之，气逆用之最佳。[11p]

    Phlegm consists of dried tangerine peel and pinellia. For qi deficiency, use ginseng and white atractylodes. For yin fire, use coptis, honeysuckle, and talc. If there is a cough with reversed flow and diarrhea, use talc, licorice, fried coptis, white peony, ginseng, white atractylodes, and dried tangerine peel, along with bamboo roof sap to take.

    Coughing and reversal is referred to in ancient times as "he" and more recently as "e," caused by cold in the stomach, where cold qi rises, making this condition very dangerous. There are also heat-related instances that present as cold damage. If there are other illnesses causing "e," use one tael of pinellia and half a tael of fresh ginger, decocted in water and taken hot; or add half a qian each of bitter orange and poria to a warming middle decoction, with one qian of pinellia; if ineffective, add ten cloves.

    For cough and reversal after vomiting or diarrhea caused by cold in the stomach, use Qianghuo and Aconite Decoction or take ten cloves and ten dried persimmon stalks chopped and decocted in water. For cough and reversal after vomiting or diarrhea due to heat in the stomach, use bamboo peel and bamboo shavings decoction.

    If there are no other illnesses and e occurs occasionally, this is due to qi reversal. In such cases, use a small amount of pinellia and poria decoction with bitter orange and pinellia. Alternatively, decoct and steep radish seeds, grind to extract the juice, and mix with wood fragrant to disperse heat, which is particularly effective for reversed qi.[11p]

    　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

    　　　　　水寒相搏

    　　哕即干呕，声更重且长耳。[食(句去口改吉)]乃胸间气塞不通。胃脉浮则为[食(句去口改吉)]，滑则为哕。皆因胃气本虚，汗下太过，或复饮冷水，水寒相搏，胃气虚逆而上，理中汤加肉桂、丁香以散寒下气，茯苓、半夏以消水。而不止者，橘皮干姜汤、橘皮竹茹汤。间有热邪壅郁，上下之气不得通者俱小柴胡加生姜和之。热甚便难者，小承气下之。便软者，诸泻心汤选用。温病发渴饮冷作哕者，升麻葛根汤加茅根。必用半夏，散结气也；用竹茹，清胃解烦也；用生姜，散逆气也。皆因气逆所致，故生姜为呕家圣药。热者乌梅代之。[12p]

    Introduction to Medicine

    By Li Chen (Ming Dynasty)

    Cold Water Clashing

    When one experiences a heaving sensation, it means dry retching, with a voice that is heavier and longer. This occurs due to a blockage of qi in the chest. If the stomach pulse is floating, it indicates a blockage; if slippery, it suggests heaving. Both conditions arise from weakened stomach qi, which may be exacerbated by excessive sweating or drinking cold water. The clash of cold water causes the stomach qi to rise abnormally. To alleviate this, one can use the "Li Zhong Tang" with added cinnamon and clove to disperse cold and reduce qi. Additionally, Poria and Banxia can help dispel water retention. If the conditions persist, one may consider using "Gui Pi Tang" or "Zhu Ru Tang."

    If there is a blockage due to heat stagnation that obstructs the upward and downward flow of qi, then "Xiao Chai Hu Tang" with fresh ginger should be included. In severe cases of constipation, the "Xiao Cheng Qi Tang" formula should be used. For soft stools, a selection of "Zhong Shi Tang" is recommended. For warm diseases that cause thirst and result in heaving, "Sheng Ma Ge Gen Tang" with added rhizoma of reed should be used. One must always incorporate Banxia to disperse qi stagnation; bamboo leaves help clear the stomach and relieve restlessness; fresh ginger disperses the rising qi. These issues arise from qi reversal, making fresh ginger an essential remedy for vomiting. If there is heat, black plum can be used as a substitute.[12p]

    　　　　　吃逆辨名

    　　旧以为咳嗽之咳，俗又以为口呃之呃。虞花溪考韵书，(食戹)与呃通，乃气逆上之名。又有以呃逆为哕者。哕出声然后吸；呃逆入声，逆尽然后呼，出入呼吸不同。兼呕哕者，本于胃；不呕哕者，本于肺。谷入于胃，胃气上注于肺，故寒气与新谷气相忤，逆而复于胃，故噫噫有声。所以丹溪力辨乃相火自脐下直上冲胸，交于厥阴，水火相搏而声作也。[13p]

    Eating Reversed and Naming

    It used to be thought that coughing referred to the cough itself, while the common view equated "呃" with the sound made when something is stuck in the throat. According to the study of rhymes by Yu Huaxi, "食戹" is associated with "呃," which refers to the rising of qi. There is also a definition of "呃" as "哕," where "哕" produces a sound before inhalation, while "呃" produces a sound after the reverse flow is complete. The processes of inhalation and exhalation differ. For those who experience both vomiting and "哕," the issue originates from the stomach; for those who do not, it stems from the lungs. When grains enter the stomach, the stomach qi rises to the lungs, leading to a conflict between cold qi and the fresh grain qi, causing it to reverse back to the stomach, resulting in audible "噫噫." Thus, Danxi emphasized that the fire from the lower abdomen directly surges up to the chest, interacting with the jueyin, causing a clash between water and fire, which produces the sound.[13p]

    　　　　　证分阴阳

    　　阳证发热，口苦胸满，脉弦数，小柴胡汤加竹茹；小便闭，加茯苓或猪苓汤。大便闭者，调胃承气汤。少阴证失下腹满便闭，或纯下清水(食戹)逆者，小承气汤。阳明身热口渴，胸满烦躁，脉洪数(食戹)逆者，火冲肺也，甘草泻心汤。　　阴证便软胃寒，或因吐下虚极恶寒脉细者，橘皮干姜汤。内寒厥冷者，羌活附子汤、丁香柿蒂散，调苏合香丸。胃寒饮水相搏者，小青龙汤去麻黄加附子。手足厥冷者，小橘皮汤。胸满虚烦者，大橘皮汤。凡(食戹)逆药中俱宜陈皮、竹茹、姜汁。此证有欲作正汗阴阳升降而然者即愈；又有食积而致者，小便闭濇及痰火上冲者。腹满不得小便，及脉见沉微散者死。其为病大同水气，表里俱有此证。[14p]

    Differentiating Between Yang and Yin Patterns

    Yang patterns present with fever, bitter mouth, chest fullness, and a wiry rapid pulse. For such symptoms, prescribe Xiaochaihu Decoction with bamboo shavings; if there is urinary retention, add Poria or use Zhu Ling Decoction. For constipation, use Tiaogui Chengqi Decoction. In cases of Shaoyin patterns with fullness in the lower abdomen and constipation, or if clear water (from food) is regurgitating, prescribe Xiao Chengqi Decoction. In Yangming patterns with fever and thirst, chest fullness, and irritability, indicated by a surging rapid pulse, this may be fire attacking the lungs, for which use Gan Cao Xie Xin Decoction.

    Yin patterns characterized by soft stools and gastric coldness, or due to extreme vomiting and diarrhea leading to aversion to cold with a thin pulse, should use Ju Pi Gan Jiang Decoction. For internal cold and cold extremities, use Qiang Huo Fu Zi Decoction or Ding Xiang Shi Di San, and adjust with Su He Xiang Wan. For gastric cold causing drinking water to clash, prescribe Xiao Qinglong Decoction, omitting Ma Huang and adding Fu Zi. For cold hands and feet, use Xiao Ju Pi Decoction. For chest fullness and weakness, use Da Ju Pi Decoction. As a rule, for food regurgitation, all remedies should include Chen Pi, bamboo shavings, and ginger juice. When symptoms arise indicating the need for proper sweating, or if Yin and Yang are rising and falling, recovery is possible; if food accumulates, leading to urinary retention and phlegm-fire rising, abdominal fullness with inability to urinate, and a sinking and faint pulse, it indicates a grim prognosis. The disease fundamentally relates to water qi, with both exterior and interior signs present.[14p]

    　　　　　病别虚实

    　　不足，因内伤脾胃及大病后胃弱，多面青、肢冷、便软；有余，因外感胃燥，及大怒大饱，多面红、肢热、便闭。有余可治，不足者危。
    　　　　　火炎阴虚

    　　火乃元气之贼。人之阴气依胃气而养，胃土受伤则木气侵之，阴火所乘，不得内守，木挟相火直冲清道而上，乃虚之甚也。　　膏粱湿热者，十味小柴胡汤吞单黄蘗丸，或调益元散。胃火善食者，小半夏汤加山栀、黄芩吐之。火盛者益元散加黄连、黄蘗。自利，更加参、朮、白芍、陈皮。　　久病滞下，及妇人产后，从脐下逆上，夜分转甚者，皆属阴虚，四物汤加知、蘗、陈皮、竹茹。
    　　　　　劳役伤脾

    　　贫苦大劳火动，浊升清陷者，补中益气汤，或合生脉散加黄蘗、附子少许。挟房劳者，琼玉膏。肾气不归元者，九味安肾丸。[15p]

    Differentiation of Illness: Deficiency and Excess

    Deficiency arises from internal injuries to the spleen and stomach or from weakness after a major illness, often presenting with a pale face, cold limbs, and loose stools. Excess is due to external factors causing dryness in the stomach or from great anger and overeating, often presenting with a red face, heat in the limbs, and constipation. Excess can be treated, but deficiency is dangerous.

    Heat from Inefficiency of Yin

    Fire is the thief of original Qi. The Yin Qi of a person is nourished by the Stomach Qi. When the stomach is harmed, the wood element invades it, the Yin fire takes advantage, unable to guard internally, and the wood carries the fire upwards, severely worsening deficiency. Those with damp-heat from rich foods can take the Ten Flavor Xiao Chai Hu Decoction along with Dan Huang Bo pills or tune with Yi Yuan Powder. For those with strong stomach fire and good appetite, use Xiao Ban Xia Decoction adding Shan Zhi, Huang Qin to induce vomiting. For excessive fire, add Huang Lian, Huang Bo to Yi Yuan Powder. For those with diarrhea or women postpartum, experiencing reversal from the navel upwards, particularly at night, all belong to Yin deficiency, needing Si Wu Decoction with added Zhi Mu, Bo He, Chen Pi, and Zhu Ru.

    Strain and Injury to the Spleen

    Severe labor and poverty cause fire to rise and turbidity to ascend, needing Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction or Sheng Mai San with a little Huang Bo and Fu Zi. For those with sexual strain, use Qiong Yu Paste. If kidney Qi does not return to the source, use Jiu Wei An Shen Pills.[15p]

    　　　　　久病

    　　久病极是危证。脉数为火，刑金必死。凡伤寒吐下及杂病久每呃逆者，皆火欲上行，为胃中寒邪所遏，故搏而有声，俱宜丁香柿蒂散、羌活附子汤、理中汤倍参。久者，三香散，或木瓜根煎汤呷之。中虚昏愦脉结者，炙甘草汤救之。
    　　　　　伤食

    　　饱食填塞，胸中失升降之道，二陈汤加枳壳、砂仁。
    　　　　　痰气

    　　痰闭于上，火动于下，无别证，忽然发呃，从胸中起者，芩连二陈汤，或祇陈皮、半夏、姜煎服，或人参芦煎汤吐之。停痰或因怒郁挟热者亦宜。盖参芦泻肺，肺衰气降而火土复位矣。　　七情气郁者，木香匀气散，用萝卜煎汤下，或苏子降气汤。
    　　　　　失下误下

    　　地道不通，因而呃逆，宜寒药下之，大柴胡汤。阳极脉微将脱者，宜凉膈散、解毒汤，养阴退阳，不可大下。　　汗吐下后，胃热未除，小柴胡加橘皮、竹茹，或橘皮竹茹汤、单泻心汤。[16p]

    Prolonged Illness

    Prolonged illness is a dangerous condition. A rapid pulse indicates fire, and if metal is affected, it is likely to be fatal. In cases of prolonged illnesses from cold damage, vomiting, or diarrhea, along with symptoms of hiccups, this indicates fire attempting to ascend, being obstructed by cold pathogens in the stomach. Therefore, it is appropriate to administer a blend of clove and persimmon calyx powder, Qianghuo Fuzi Decoction, or a modified Li Zhong Decoction with increased ginseng. For long-standing cases, use Sanxiang Powder or decoction of papaya root. If there is middle vacuity, stupor, and a knotty pulse, use the honey-fried licorice decoction to rescue.

    Food Stagnation

    When the stomach is overly full, the pathway of ascension and descent is obstructed. One should use the Er Chen Decoction with added bitter orange peel and sand ginger.

    Phlegm and Qi

    When phlegm is obstructed above and fire is activated below, without other symptoms, and if hiccups suddenly arise from the chest, one should use the Qinjian Er Chen Decoction, or simply take decoctions of tangerine peel, pinellia, and ginger. Alternatively, ginseng and reed decoction can be used for expulsion. Stagnant phlegm due to anger and heat is also manageable. Ginseng and reed clear the lungs, allowing the lungs to regain function and restoring fire and earth to their proper places. If one is affected by emotional distress, the Mukxiang Yungqi Powder should be used, administered with radish decoction, or the Suzi Jiangqi Decoction.

    Mismanaged Downward Movement

    When the pathways are obstructed, leading to hiccups, cold medicines should be administered. Da Chai Hu Decoction is appropriate. If the pulse is excessively weak and on the verge of collapse, it is necessary to use Liang Ge Powder or Detoxification Decoction to nourish yin and diminish yang; large purgation should be avoided. After sweating, vomiting, and purging, if stomach heat remains, one can take Xiao Chai Hu Decoction combined with tangerine peel and bamboo shavings, or decoctions of tangerine peel and bamboo shavings, or a single heart-purge decoction.[16p]

    　　　　　治法

    　　平人食物太速，饮水入肺，喜笑太多，亦属有余。食呃笑呃，以纸捻刺鼻取嚏，或久闭气可止。水呃，小陷胸汤、小青龙汤去麻黄，清之利之而已。大凡汗吐下服凉药过多者，当温补；脾胃阴火上冲者，当平补；挟热者，宜凉补。　《局方》率用丁附温暖助火，损不足而益有余，宜乎呃逆之必死也。
    　　　　证治要诀 【明　戴思恭】

    　　　　　总论证治

    　　伤寒咳逆，仲景谓咳逆为哕，有阴阳二证。阴证乃胃寒所生。亦有初本是热，因大发汗后复吐下之，攻热太过，以致胃寒。因寒而咳逆者，橘皮干姜汤，或半夏生姜汤。咳逆，就桔梗枳壳汤中加半夏、陈皮等分，生姜十片煎；亦治阴证咳逆。阳证咳逆乃胃家热，小柴胡汤、橘皮竹茹汤。阳证咳逆而又兼腹痛者，问其前后知何部不利，前部猪苓汤，后部调胃承气汤。[17p]

    Treatment Methods

    When a person eats too quickly, inhales water into the lungs, or laughs excessively, it is considered excess. If there is belching from eating or laughing, one can use paper twists to stimulate the nose for a sneeze, or holding their breath for a long time may stop it. For water-related belching, one may use Xiao Xian(xiong) Tang or Xiao Qing Long Tang without Ma Huang, simply to clear and resolve. Generally, if one has sweated, vomited, or taken too many cooling medications, they should take warming tonics; if there is upward rising of spleen and stomach yin fire, they should take balanced tonics; if there is heat present, cooling tonics are appropriate. "Jufang" usually employs Dingfu to warm and assist the fire, diminishing insufficiencies and benefiting the excess, thus it is likely that belching and counterflow will inevitably lead to death.

    Summary of Diagnosis and Treatment

    For cold damage with cough and counterflow, Zhongjing refers to cough counterflow as "yi," with two types of conditions: yin and yang. The yin condition arises from cold in the stomach. There may also be cases where the initial condition was heat, but excessive sweating later led to vomiting and purging, attacking heat too vigorously, leading to stomach cold. For cough and counterflow due to cold, use dried tangerine peel and ginger decoction, or half summer and ginger decoction. For cough and counterflow, add half summer and aged tangerine peel in equal parts to the decoction of platycodon and bitter orange, and boil with ten slices of ginger; this also treats the yin condition of cough and counterflow. The yang condition of cough counterflow results from heat in the stomach, treated with Xiao Chai Hu Tang or tangerine peel and bamboo leaf decoction. If the yang condition of cough counterflow also includes abdominal pain, inquire about the location of the discomfort. If it is in the front, use Zhu Ling Tang; if in the back, use Tiao Wei Cheng Qi Tang.[17p]

    亦有无病偶然致呃，此缘气逆而生，重者，或经一二日，宜小半夏茯苓汤加枳实半夏汤，或用煎汤泡萝卜子研取汁，调木香调气散，乘热服，逆气用之最佳。若胃中寒甚，咳逆不已，或复加以呕吐，轻剂不能取效，宜丁香煮散，及以附子粳米汤，增炒川椒、丁香，每服各十粒。　　胃实即噫，胃虚即哕。逆者胃中虚，膈上热也。咳逆为病，古谓之哕，近谓之呃，乃胃寒所生，寒气自逆而呃上，此证最危。间有热呃已见伤寒证。其有他病发呃者，皆属寒，宜用半夏一两，生姜两半，水一碗，煎半碗，热服；或用丁香十粒，柿蒂十个，切碎，白水盏半煎；或理中汤加枳壳、茯苓各半钱，半夏一钱，不效，更加丁香十粒。[18p]

    There are cases where one experiences belching without illness, which is due to the reversal of qi. In severe cases, it may persist for a day or two. It is advisable to use a small amount of Banxia Fuling Decoction, adding Zhi Shi and Banxia, or to use a decoction to soak radish seeds, extract the juice, and adjust with Mu Xiang to regulate the qi, taking it warm, which is best for combating reversed qi. If there is severe cold in the stomach, causing persistent cough and possibly vomiting, and light remedies do not take effect, one should use clove decoction, and add Fuzi and glutinous rice decoction, increasing the amounts of stir-fried Sichuan pepper and cloves to ten each per dose.

    When the stomach is full, it leads to belching; when it is deficient, it causes "huò" (a type of prolonged belching). Reversal indicates insufficiency in the stomach and excess heat above the diaphragm. Coughing with reversal is a condition referred to in ancient texts as "huò" and more recently as "è," stemming from cold in the stomach, causing the cold qi to reverse and lead to belching, which is the most serious symptom. Occasionally, there may be heated belching seen in cases of febrile diseases. If belching occurs due to other illnesses, it still relates to cold, and the remedy should be one liang of Banxia, two halves of fresh ginger, and one bowl of water, decocted to half a bowl and taken hot; alternatively, take ten cloves and ten cut persimmon stems, boiled in half a bowl of white water. If ineffective, one may add an additional ten cloves to a modified Li Zhong Decoction with half a qian of Zhi Ke and Fuling, and one qian of Banxia.[18p]

    　　　　伤寒六书 【明　陶华】

    　　　　　论证辨名

    　　哕即干呕之甚者，非比干呕则有声，浊恶而长，皆有声而无物也。盖因胃气本虚，因汗下太过，或恣饮冷水，水寒相搏，虚逆而成也。又有热气拥郁，上下不得通而哕者，轻则和解疏利，重则温散。哕而腹满，大便不利，先用半夏生姜汤，次用小承气；小便不利者，猪苓汤。哕不止者，干姜橘皮汤。温病有热，暴饮冷水作哕，茅根干葛汤。哕家若不尿而哕者，则病笃矣。　　夫咳逆者，俗谓之呃忒是也。纔发声于喉间则遽止，呃呃然连续数声，然而短促不长。古人谓之哕者，非也。哕与干呕无异，但其声浊恶而长，然皆有声而无物。病至于哕则危，难治矣。[19p]

    Shāng Hán Liù Shū | Ming Táo Hua

    Discussion on Evidence and Distinction of Names

    "Huò" refers to a severe form of dry heaving, which differs from regular dry heaving in that it is accompanied by sound, is clamorous and prolonged, producing sound without substance. This occurs due to the inherent weakness of the stomach qi, often exacerbated by excessive sweating, drinking too much cold water, or cold water clashing against internal cold, leading to a pathological reversal. Additionally, if heat qi accumulates, obstructing passage up and down, it may also cause "huò". In mild cases, it can be alleviated with harmonizing and dispersing methods; in severe cases, warming and dispersing measures are needed. If "huò" is accompanied by abdominal fullness and difficulty in defecation, first administer a half summer ginger decoction, then proceed with a small purgative. If urinary output is insufficient, use a pigweed decoction. Should "huò" persist, apply a ginger and tangerine peel decoction. For febrile conditions with heat, if "huò" arises from excessive cold water intake, a rehmannia and kudzu decoction is indicated. If "huò" occurs without urination, it indicates a grave condition.

    As for coughing reversely, it is commonly referred to as "è tè" in vernacular. The sound may just begin in the throat and then abruptly stop, resulting in short, consecutive sounds that are fleeting. The ancients distinguished this as "huò", but that is incorrect. "Huò" is not different from dry heaving; the only distinction is that it produces a prolonged, clamorous sound without substance. When the illness progresses to "huò", it becomes critical and difficult to treat.[19p]

    大抵[食(句去口改吉)]者但胸间气塞不得下通，哕则恶浊之声达于外，故二者相近，盖因胃气本虚，汗下太过，或复饮水，水寒相搏，虚逆而成。经曰：阳脉浮则为气[食(句去口改吉)]，又曰脉滑则为哕。此为医咎，责虚取实之过也。又有热气壅郁，上下气不得通而哕者，轻则和解之，通利之，甚则温散之。设若不尿腹满而哕者，咳逆脉散而无伦者，虽神医不能措手，与伤寒咳而气逆者又不同也。若将吃忒紊于哕与咳而气逆，则误人多矣。临病之际，宜明辨之。咳逆大便少，与大承气汤下之，盖由热气冲格脾肺故耳。若便软，泻心汤，胃气虚而冲脉逆也。若脉散者不治。咳逆潮热，小柴胡加橘皮生姜汤。　　伤寒或汗下太过，或恣饮冷水，水寒相搏，虚逆声浊恶而长，名哕，此与干呕不相类，轻则和解疏利，重则温散。[20p]

    Generally, when there is obstruction in the chest that prevents downward flow, it leads to the expulsion of a rough sound externally. Thus, these two conditions are similar, arising from the original weakness of the stomach qi, excessive sweating, or further drinking of cold water, which clashes with the coldness, resulting in a reversal of the qi. The texts say: when the yang pulse is floating, it indicates obstruction; and when the pulse is slippery, it signifies a rough sound. This is a medical fault, blaming weakness for taking too much from the reality.

    There is also the possibility of heat qi being trapped, preventing the qi from circulating properly, which may cause a rough sound. For mild cases, harmonizing and promoting circulation may suffice; for severe cases, warmth and dispersion are necessary.

    If, on the other hand, there is no urination and the abdomen is distended, accompanied by a rough sound, and if there is a scattered pulse without coherence, even a divine physician may not be able to intervene effectively; this condition differs from that of cold damage with a rough sound and reversed qi. If one incorrectly attributes rough sounds and coughing to reversed qi, it would lead to great mistakes. Therefore, it is important to distinguish clearly when encountering illness.

    In cases with reversed coughing and little bowel movement, one should use the major purging decoction. This is due to heat qi colliding with the spleen and lungs. If the stool is soft, one would use the heart-purging decoction to combat the reversal of stomach qi. If the pulse is scattered, it should not be treated. For reversed coughing with mild fever, one can use Xiao Chai Hu Tang with tangerine peel and fresh ginger.

    In instances of cold damage, there may be excessive sweating or indulgence in cold water, leading to the clash of coldness and the rough, unpleasant, prolonged sound known as a rough sound, which is not the same as dry heaving. For mild cases, harmonizing and promoting circulation may suffice; for severe cases, warmth and dispersion are necessary.[20p]

    　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

    　　　　　证有所别

    　　咳逆乃干咳之渐进，无痰有声，连连不绝。其气自丹田而逆上，出于咽喉，如有所击逆而然也。亦有咳声出咽，复有还声吸入咽内，此所以为咳逆证也。呃逆者，即下文云入声是也。有咳呃兼声击发，连续千万之声而不已者，服药不效，即用吐法，吐出痰涎立已。若哕者乃出声也，声尽然后吸，病本于胃，于呕吐门中已详言之，此不复及。呃逆者，入声也，气逆入喉，逆声尽然后呼也，病本于肺，其出入呼吸，大不相同，何难辨哉！[21p]

    Ancient and Modern Medical Principles
    (Ming Dynasty - Xu Chunfu)

    Distinctions in Symptoms

    Coughing and reverse cough signify a progressive dry cough, characterized by sound without phlegm, continuous and unending. The energy rises from the lower abdomen and ascends, exiting through the throat, as if struck and causing the reverse effect. There are also instances where the cough emits from the throat, followed by a sound that draws back into the throat, which is what constitutes the reverse cough symptom. Hiccups refer to a sound entering the throat. If there are both coughing and hiccuping sounds striking forth, persistent and in the tens of thousands without cessation, and medication proves ineffective, then the method of inducing vomiting should be employed to expel phlegm and saliva immediately. Hiccups, on the other hand, produce a sound exiting, and the sound ceases before inhalation; the root of this occurs in the stomach, elaborated upon in discussions of vomiting, thus will not be revisited here. Hiccups are characterized by an inward sound, where the energy reverses into the throat, and the sound ceases before exhalation; the root of this lies in the lungs, and their inhalation and exhalation differ greatly, making them easy to distinguish.[21p]

    　　　　　咳逆属火

    　　《活人书》云：咳逆，仲景所谓哕是也。哕为胃寒所生。伤寒本虚，攻其热必哕。又云：伤寒大吐下之，极虚后汗出者，因得哕，所以然者，胃气虚寒故也，宜橘皮干姜汤、羌活附子汤、半夏生姜汤、退阴散之属主之。此仲景治哕之方也。《活人书》误以咳为哕，故以热作寒治。仲景之言哕，非以为咳逆之谓也，咳逆从热而哕从寒。《活人》以咳逆为哕，夫安得不用热药？盖辨证一差，故其用药必反，若非东垣力辨其失，后学将孰　而知之？[22p]

    Coughing and Reflux Belong to Heat

    The "Book of Living" states: Coughing and reflux refer to what Zhong Jing called regurgitation. Regurgitation arises from stomach cold. When a febrile disease is fundamentally deficient, attacking its heat will inevitably lead to regurgitation. It also mentions that after severe vomiting and purging in a febrile disease, if one subsequently sweats profusely, regurgitation arises because of the deficiency and coldness of stomach qi. Therefore, one should use remedies such as dried tangerine peel and ginger decoction, Qianghuo and Aconite decoction, Banxia and ginger decoction, or the Retreating Yin powder. These are Zhong Jing's methods for treating regurgitation. The "Book of Living" mistakenly equates cough and reflux, thus treating heat as if it were cold. Zhong Jing's discussion of regurgitation does not imply it is the same as coughing and reflux; the former arises from cold while the latter comes from heat. Since the "Book of Living" regards coughing and reflux as the same, how can one not use heating medicines? The differentiation of syndromes is critical; thus, the choice of remedies must be precise. If it were not for Dongyuan's diligent clarification of these errors, how would subsequent scholars come to understand this?[22p]

    　　　　　病要分标别本

    　　东垣云：《活人书》以咳逆为哕，谓若可下之，宜调胃承气汤。是因邪气在胃，故断为哕，是则然矣。抑不思咳逆是阳明失下传手太阴。《活人书》言其火之本，不言其火之标，炎上至极高之分而咳逆也。合而观之，哕与咳逆同一热也。分而言之，哕为本，为胆、为胃、为中；咳逆为标，为心、为肺、为上。若标因应见上，当其标，不必名哕。哕不言作哕，使后人一见胆胃本而不见心肺标也。[23p]

    The Illness Must Be Distinguished Between Root and Branch

    Dong Yuan said: In the "Living Human Book," cough and reverse flow are considered a type of belching, suggesting that if it can be treated with purgatives, it is advisable to use the Gui Cheng Qi Decoction. This is because the evil qi resides in the stomach, thus it is identified as belching, which is indeed the case. However, one should not forget that cough and reverse flow indicate that the Yangming has lost its downward transmission to the Taiyin. The "Living Human Book" discusses the root of fire but does not address its branch; it mentions that fire rises to an extreme height leading to cough and reverse flow. Viewed together, belching and cough are manifestations of the same heat. Specifically, belching pertains to the root, associated with the gallbladder, stomach, and the middle; whereas cough pertains to the branch, associated with the heart, lungs, and the upper. If the branch is evident above, then it is rightfully called a branch and does not need to be termed belching. If it is not indicated that it is belching, later generations might only notice the gallbladder and stomach as the root, neglecting the heart and lung as the branch.[23p]

    　　　　　治宜降火顺气

    　　咳逆证古方多作寒气，故用丁香、柿蒂、姜、附热剂，此亦一偏也。咳逆有虚、有实、有火。今其气自下冲上而作声，非气而何？大抵伤寒杂证，汗吐下后，过服凉剂，胃气虚寒者，或亦有之。惟此可从温补，亦不宜用热剂。除此之外，就因病后，必是发热失于汗下，热郁既久，以致阴虚，须汗下之，亦失其时，致火亢极，故虽退热之后，尚有火伏阴中，而乘胃虚冲上，连声逆吸而为咳(食戹)之证也。竹茹、麦门冬、橘皮之类，便秘以承气汤下之。[24p]

    The treatment should reduce internal heat and harmonize the Qi.

    Coughing with a reverse flow often holds characteristics of coldness in ancient formulas. Therefore, ingredients such as clove, persimmon stem, ginger, and warming medicines are used, although this may be one-sided. Coughing with a reverse flow can be due to deficiency, excess, or heat. When the Qi forcefully rises from below to create sound, what else could it be? Generally, in cases of epidemic fevers, after sweating, vomiting, and purging, overusing cooling medications may lead to weak and cold stomach Qi. This could also occur. In such instances, one must use warming tonics, and not heat-inducing medicines.

    Aside from this, if it occurs after an illness, it is often due to prolonged heat when sweating was not adequately achieved, causing enduring heat stagnation, leading to Yin deficiency. If one sweats and purges at the wrong time, it results in excessive heat, so even after the fever has subsided, there can still be heat lurking in the Yin, rising in combination with weak stomach Qi, creating a sound that results in cough (food stagnation) symptoms. Ingredients such as bamboo shavings, ophiopogon, and orange peel can help alleviate constipation with purgative decoctions.[24p]

    　　　　　吐下法效速

    　　凡有忍气郁结积怒之人，并不得行其志者，多有咳逆之证，药以降火清痰顺气；不效者，必须吐法，以人参芦煎汤，人煨盐少许饮之，少顷探吐胶固痰涎，其咳立已。　　实者，病伤寒失下，大便秘结而咳逆，速以寒剂下之。若因饮食过伤，或因痰饮停宿，或因暴怒气逆而得此证，皆为形气俱实，用子和涌法极效，人参芦尤佳。咳逆要审有余不足。如丹溪治一老人患滞下后发咳逆，用参朮汤下大补丸而愈。又治一女子，怒后作食(食戹)，用人参芦吐之而愈。[25p]

    Method of Inducing Vomiting

    For those who bear repressed anger and are unable to act on their will, many exhibit symptoms of coughing and rebellion. The remedy involves clearing heat, purging phlegm, and soothing qi; if this proves ineffective, it is essential to induce vomiting. This can be done using a decoction of ginseng and reed, with a small amount of salt, which should be consumed. After a little while, inducing vomiting will expel the thick phlegm and saliva, and the cough will cease.

    In cases where there is a substantial condition caused by an external cold leading to a lack of downward movement, resulting in constipation and cough, it is urgent to use cold medicines for purging. If the issue arises from excessive food intake, from phlegm or fluid stagnation, or due to violent anger and qi rebellion, it is all considered a substantial condition. In such cases, the combination of gentle purging methods, especially using ginseng and reed, is particularly effective.

    Cough and rebellion must be assessed for excess or deficiency. For instance, Danxi treated an elderly man who developed cough after constipation with ginseng and atractylodes decoction, along with a major supplement pill, and he recovered. Similarly, he treated a woman who experienced food-related issues after becoming angry by inducing vomiting with ginseng and reed, which resulted in her recovery.[25p]

    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　总论

    　　呃逆即《内经》所谓哕也。或曰：成无己、许学士固以哕为呃逆，然东垣、海藏又以哕为干呕，陈无择又以哕名咳逆，诸论不同，今子独取成许二家之说何也？曰：哕义具在《内经》，顾诸家不察耳。按《灵枢》杂病篇末云：哕，以草刺鼻嚏嚏而已；无息而疾迎引之，立已；大惊之亦可已。详此经文三法，正乃治呃逆之法。按呃逆用纸捻刺鼻便嚏，嚏则呃逆立止；或闭口鼻气，使之无息亦立已；或作冤盗贼大惊骇之，亦已。此予所以取成、许二家之论哕为呃逆为得经旨也。若以哕为干呕，设使干呕之人，或使之嚏，或使之无息，或使之大惊，其干呕能立已乎？哕非干呕也明矣！若以哕名咳逆，按《内经》生气通天论曰：秋伤于湿，上逆而咳。阴阳应象论曰：秋伤于湿，冬生咳嗽。[26p]

    Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment
    (Ming Dynasty, Wang Kengtang)

    General Discussion

    Erni, which is referred to as "he" in the “Inner Canon,” has varying interpretations. Some say Cheng Wujia and Xu Xueshi consider “he” to be erni, while Dongyuan and Haizang regard it as dry retching, and Chen Wuze names it coughing reverse. There are different opinions among scholars; why do you alone adopt the views of Cheng and Xu? The meaning of “he” is clearly stated in the “Inner Canon,” but various schools overlook this. According to the end of the miscellaneous diseases chapter in the “Spiritual Pivot,” “he” is merely caused by a tickling sensation in the nose, leading to sneezing; there are methods that can suddenly stop it. Similarly, if one is startled, it can also be alleviated. Examining these three methods from the text reveals that they are indeed treatments for erni.

    For erni, pricking the nose with a piece of paper leads to sneezing, and the sneezing will immediately stop the erni; another method is to close the mouth and restrict the breathing to stop it; or one can use a great shock from a thief or robber to achieve the same result. This is why I adopt the interpretation of “he” as erni by Cheng and Xu, for it aligns with the essence of the text. If one considers “he” as dry retching, could dry retching be stopped by sneezing, holding one’s breath, or being startled? It is clear that “he” is not dry retching!

    As for the interpretation of “he” as coughing reverse, according to the “Inner Canon,” it states: "In autumn, damage from dampness causes upward rebellion and coughing." The theory of yin and yang correspondence also indicates: "In autumn, damage from dampness leads to coughing in winter."[26p]

    以此论之，则咳逆为咳嗽无疑，以春夏冬三时比例自见。孙真人《千金》曰：欬逆者嗽也。本自明白，后人不知何以将咳逆误作呃逆，失之远矣！　　刘宗厚曰：呃逆一证，有虚有实，有火有痰有水气，不可专作寒论。盖伤寒发汗吐下之后，与泻利日久及大病后、妇人产后有此者，皆脾胃气血大虚之故也。若平人食入太速，而气噎，或饮水喜笑错喉而气抢，或因痰水停隔心中，或因暴怒气逆痰厥，或伤寒热病失下而有此者，则皆属实也。夫水性润下，火性炎上，今其气自下冲上，非火而何？大抵治法虚则补之，虚中须分寒热。如因汗吐下后误服寒凉过多，当以温补之；如脾胃阴虚火逆上冲，当以平补之；挟热者，凉而补之。若夫实者如伤寒失下，地道不通，因而呃逆，当以寒下之。如痰饮停畜，或暴怒气逆痰厥，此等必形气俱实，别无恶候，当随其邪之所在，涌之、泄之、清之、利之也。[27p]

    In this discussion, it is clear that "ke ni" refers to coughing, as evident from its comparison throughout the three seasons of spring, summer, and winter. The Daoist Master Sun said in "Qianjin": "Ke ni" is certainly a cough. This is self-evident, but later generations have mistakenly interpreted "ke ni" as "e ni," which is a significant error.

    Liu Zonghou mentioned: The symptom of "e ni" can be either due to deficiency or excess, and can involve heat, phlegm, or water qi; it should not be exclusively categorized under cold conditions. For instance, after sweating, vomiting, or purging due to a cold, and in cases of prolonged diarrhea or after a serious illness, or postpartum conditions in women, such symptoms arise from severe deficiency of the spleen and stomach qi and blood.

    If a healthy person eats too quickly, causing qi to get stuck, or if they drink water and laugh, leading to choking, or if phlegm-water obstructs the heart, or if anger causes qi to rebel and phlegm to ascend, or if it occurs post-illness due to heat without proper purging, all these are classified as excess conditions. Water is moist and descendent, while fire is hot and ascendant; if the qi is pushing upward from below, what else could it be but fire? Generally, the treatment for deficiency is to tonify it, but within deficiency, one must differentiate between cold and heat. If due to excessive consumption of cold after sweating, vomiting, or purging, it should be treated with warming tonics; if due to deficiency-heat from the spleen and stomach, it should be treated with harmonizing tonics; if heat is present, cool and tonify.

    In contrast, conditions like excess from cold in cases of illness leading to "e ni" necessitate cooling and purging. Similarly, when phlegm-water stagnates, or if overwhelming anger leads to rebellious qi and phlegm, these symptoms must be characterized by substantial excess qi, with no other adverse signs. The treatment should target the location of the pathogenic qi by inducing, purging, clearing, or draining as needed.[27p]

    　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

    　　　　　论证

    　　呃逆一证，古无是名，其在《内经》本谓之哕，因其呃呃连声，故今以呃逆名之，于义亦妥。观《内经》治哕之法，以草刺鼻而嚏，及气息迎引、大惊之类，是皆治呃之法。此哕本呃逆，无待辨也。自孙真人云：遍寻方论无比名，遂以咳逆为哕，因致后世讹传，乃以咳逆、干呕、噫气之类，互相淆乱，自唐迄今矣。此名之不可不察，亦不可不正也。　　咳逆之名，原出《内经》，本以咳嗽气逆者为言。如气交变大论曰：岁金太过，甚则喘咳逆气。此因喘咳以致气逆，故云咳逆气也。又曰：欬逆甚而血溢。[28p]

    Discussion on Reversal of Qi

    The term "reversal of qi" did not exist in ancient texts; in the "Inner Canon," it was originally called "hiccup," named for the repeated sound it produces, hence it is now referred to as reversal of qi, which is also appropriate in meaning. Observing the methods to treat hiccups in the "Inner Canon," one uses herbs to stimulate the nose to induce sneezing, or applies techniques like breath manipulation and shock, which are all remedies for hiccups. This hiccup is fundamentally the reversal of qi, and there is no need for further distinction.

    Master Sun stated: Amidst the extensive search for methods, no similar name was found, thus he equated "coughing and reversal" with hiccups. This led to subsequent generations misinterpreting and confusing "coughing," "dry heaving," and "belching" since the Tang Dynasty. Such terminologies must be examined and corrected.

    The term "coughing and reversal" originally comes from the "Inner Canon," where it refers to the phenomenon of coughing accompanied by reversed qi. For instance, in the "Great Treatise on Changes," it states that when the metal element (autumn) is excessive, it can lead to coughing and reversed qi. This indicates that coughing results in reversed qi, thus it is called "reversed qi." It also mentions: "When coughing and reversal worsen, blood may overflow."[28p]

    正以咳逆不止而血随气溢，则病之常也，未闻以呃逆而见血者也。即如六元正纪大论云；金郁之发，民病咳逆者，亦是此意。此欬逆之非呃逆，亦甚明矣。而今后世诸公乃悉以哕为咳逆，岂皆未之详察耶？及观丹溪之言，在《纂要》则曰：孙真人误以哕为咳逆，是谓哕非咳逆也。在《心法附录》则曰：咳逆为病，古谓之哕，近谓之呃，此又谓哕即咳逆也。在呕吐门则又曰：有声有物谓之呕吐，有声无物谓之哕，此又以干呕为哕也。前后不一，何其自谬若此！再如海藏、河间诸公，有以哕为干呕者，有以咳逆为噫者，总皆谬矣。[29p]

    It is common for a condition where persistent cough and reverse flow of qi lead to blood, but it has not been heard of that coughing with reverse flow results in blood. Just as the Great Discussion on the Six Origins states: when there is metal distress, people suffering from cough with reverse flow relates to this notion. It is also clear that this cough is not the same as the reverse flow of qi. However, in later generations, some officials have defined reverse flow only as a type of cough, which shows they have not thoroughly examined the matter.

    Observing the words of Danxi, in "Essentials Compilation," it is stated: Master Sun mistakenly identified reverse flow as a cough, indicating that reverse flow is not cough. In the "Heart Methods Appendix," it is stated: cough with reverse flow means the ancient term was "哕" (huè), a recent term being "呃" (è), suggesting again that "哕" is indeed cough with reverse flow. The section on vomiting states: if there is sound and material, it is called vomiting; if there is sound without material, it is called "哕." Thus, dry heaving is also categorized as "哕." The inconsistencies here are quite mistaken! Furthermore, some officials from Haizang and Hejian view "哕" as dry heaving while considering cough with reverse flow as "噫" (yī), which is all erroneous.[29p]

    盖呕即吐之类，但吐而无物者曰呕，呕而有物者曰吐；腹胀嗳气者曰噫，逆气自下而上者亦曰噫。此四者之辨，自有正名，顾可纷纷若是乎？兹余析而判之曰：哕者呃逆也，非咳逆也。欬逆者，欬嗽之甚者也，非呃逆也。干呕者，无物之吐即呕也，非哕也。噫者，饱食之息，即暧气也，非咳逆也。后人但以此为鉴，则异说之疑可尽释矣。　　呃逆证有伤寒，有杂证，其在古人则悉以虚寒为言。惟丹溪引《内经》之言曰：诸逆冲上，皆属于火。病人见此，似为死证。然亦有实者，不可不知。[30p]

    The act of nausea can be categorized into two types: when one vomits without any material, it is called "nausea," and when one vomits with material, it is called "vomiting." The condition of abdominal distension and belching is referred to as "regurgitating," while the upward movement of qi from below is also called "regurgitating." These four terms have distinct meanings and proper names; can they be confused in this way? Therefore, I analyze and clarify them: belching refers to the regurgitation of food, not a cough reflex. A severe cough reflex is referred to as a strong cough, not regurgitation. Dry heaving is empty vomiting, which is nausea, not belching. Regurgitating refers to the breath after a full meal, which is warm qi, not a cough reflex. If later generations take this as a guide, then the doubts arising from differing opinions can be resolved. The symptoms of regurgitation can be associated with typhoid fever or other mixed conditions; in ancient texts, they were all regarded as manifestations of cold deficiency. However, Danxi cites the Neijing, stating that all regurgitations that rise upward belong to fire. When patients exhibit this, it may seem like a critical condition. Yet, there are also cases of true excess that should not be overlooked.[30p]

    余向见此说，疑其与古人相左，不以为然，盖亦谓此证必属虚寒，何有实热？兹及晚年历验，始有定见，乃知丹溪此言为不诬也。虽其中寒热虚实，亦有不同，然致呃之因，总由气逆，气逆于下，则直冲于上，无气则无呃，无阳亦无呃，故致之之因，所以必由气也。欲得其象，不见雨中之雷，水中之浡乎？夫阳为阴蔽，所以为雷，而轰轰不已者，此火为雷之本，而火即气也；气为水覆，所以为浡，而汨汨不已者，此气为浡之本，而气即阳也。然病在气分，本非一端，而呃之大要，亦惟三者而已，则一曰寒、二曰热、三曰虚脱。寒呃可温可散，寒去则气自舒也；热呃可降可清，火静而气自平也。惟虚脱之呃，则诚危殆之证，其或免者亦万幸矣。[31p]

    I once saw this statement and doubted that it contradicted ancient thinkers, thinking it incorrect, as I believed this evidence must pertain to the condition of coldness and not to actual heat. However, with my experiences in later years, I gained a definitive understanding and realized that Danxi's words were indeed not false. Although the distinctions between cold and heat, void and substance vary, the fundamental cause of a cough is always due to reversed Qi. When Qi is reversed from below, it rushes upward; without Qi, there is no cough, and without Yang, there is also no cough. Thus, the cause must be related to Qi. If one wishes to understand its manifestations, do we not witness thunder in the rain or splashing in the water? For Yang is obscured by Yin, giving rise to thunder, which roars unceasingly; this fire is the origin of thunder, and fire is precisely Qi. Similarly, Qi is concealed by water, giving rise to splashing, which flows continuously; this Qi is the origin of splashing, and Qi is indeed Yang. However, when the illness resides in the Qi aspect, it is not just one side; the primary causes of coughing are merely three: first, cold; second, heat; and third, deficiency and collapse. A cough from cold can be warmed or dispersed, and once the cold leaves, the Qi will naturally ease. A cough from heat can be lowered or cleared, and when the fire calms, the Qi will stabilize. Yet a cough arising from deficiency and collapse is indeed a perilous sign, and those who escape from it are exceedingly fortunate.[31p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　凡杂证之呃，虽由气逆，然有兼寒者，有兼热者，有因食滞而逆者，有因气滞而逆者，有因中气虚而逆者，有因阴气竭而逆者，但察其因而治其气，自无不愈。若轻易之呃，或偶然之逆，气顺则已，本不必治。惟屡呃为患，及呃之甚者，必其气有大逆，或脾肾元气大有亏竭而然。然实证不难治，而惟元气败竭者，乃最危之候也。　　寒滞为呃者，或以风寒，或以生冷，或其脏气本寒，偶有所逆，皆能致呃，但去其蔽抑之寒而呃自止，宜橘皮汤、三因丁香散，或二陈汤加生姜五七片，或佐关煎，或甘草干姜汤、橘皮干姜汤之类，皆可酌用。若寒之甚者，浆水散或四逆汤。[32p]

    On Cough

    In cases of mixed symptoms of hiccup, although they arise from reversed qi, there are those with a combination of cold, those with a combination of heat, those due to food stagnation causing reversal, those due to qi stagnation causing reversal, those due to deficiency of the middle qi causing reversal, and those due to depletion of yin qi causing reversal. However, by observing the causes and treating the qi, there will be no cases that cannot be cured. If hiccups are mild or occur occasionally, and the qi is flowing smoothly, there is no need for treatment. Only when hiccups are frequent or severe must one consider that the qi is greatly reversed, or there is significant depletion of the spleen and kidney's vital energy.

    Actual patterns of symptoms are not difficult to treat, but depletion of the vital energy is the most dangerous condition. When cold stagnation causes hiccups, it might be due to wind-cold, consumption of raw or cold foods, or the inherent cold nature of the internal organs that occasionally leads to reversal. In such cases, removing the obstruction and suppressing the cold will stop the hiccup. Suitable remedies include tangerine peel soup, San Yin clove powder, or Er Chen decoction with five to seven slices of fresh ginger, or combined with other formulas such as Guanjian decoction or licorice and dried ginger soup, or tangerine peel and dried ginger soup. When the cold is severe, use Jiangshui powder or Si Ni decoction.[32p]

    　　胃火为呃者，其证极多，但察其脉见滑实而形气不虚，胸膈有滞，或大便坚实，或不行者，皆其胃中有火，所以上冲为呃。但降其火，其呃自止，惟安胃饮为最妙。余尝治愈多人，皆此证也。　　气逆为哕而兼胀闷者，宜加减二陈汤加乌药，或宝鉴丁香柿蒂散，或羌活附子汤，或神香散。　　食滞而呃者，宜加减二陈加山楂、白芥子、乌药之属，或用大和中饮加干姜、木香。　　中焦脾胃虚寒，气逆为呃者，宜理中汤加丁香，或温胃饮加丁香。若因劳倦内伤而致呃逆者，宜补中益气汤加丁香。凡中焦寒甚者，多由脾胃气虚而然。盖脾胃不虚，则寒亦不甚，故治寒者，当以脾气为主。若无热者，宜生姜、半夏、丁香、柿蒂、白朮、肉桂之类皆可。吐利后胃气微虚，或兼膈热而呃者，宜橘皮竹茹汤酌用。　　下焦虚寒者，其肝肾生气之原不能畅达，故凡虚弱之人多见呃逆，正以元阳无力，易为抑遏而然。[33p]

    Stomach fire causes hiccups, and its symptoms are quite numerous. However, upon examining the pulse, if it is slippery and solid while the body is not deficient in energy, and there is stagnation in the chest and diaphragm, or if the stools are hard or do not pass, it indicates that there is fire in the stomach, which causes the hiccups. By reducing this fire, the hiccups will naturally stop, and using “An Wei Drink” is most effective. I have cured many people with these symptoms.

    For hiccups accompanied by bloating due to qi counterflow, it is advisable to use a modified Er Chen Decoction with added Wu Yao, or Baoguan Dingxiang Shidi Powder, or Qiang Huo Fu Zi Decoction, or Shen Xiang Powder.

    If hiccups are caused by food stagnation, one should use a modified Er Chen Decoction with added Hawthorn, White Mustard Seed, and Wu Yao, or employ Da He Zhong Drink with added Dried Ginger and Mu Xiang.

    For those with deficiency cold in the middle burner (spleen and stomach) and hiccups caused by qi counterflow, one should use a modified Li Zhong Decoction with added Dingxiang, or Warm Stomach Drink with Dingxiang. If hiccups are a result of internal injury from overwork and fatigue, one should use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with added Dingxiang. Generally, severe cold in the middle burner stems from deficiency in spleen and stomach qi. If the spleen and stomach are not deficient, then the cold will not be severe; hence, when treating cold, the focus should be on spleen qi. If there is no heat present, ingredients like Fresh Ginger, Ban Xia, Dingxiang, Shidi, Bai Zhu, and Cinnamon can be used.

    After vomiting or purging when the stomach qi is slightly deficient, or if hiccups are accompanied by heat in the diaphragm, one should use Tangerine Peel and Bamboo Shavings Decoction suitably.

    For deficiency cold in the lower burner, the liver and kidney’s ability to produce vital energy is impaired, hence hiccups are commonly seen in weak individuals due to insufficient original yang, which is easily suppressed.[33p]

    此呃逆之本，多在肾中，故余制归气饮主之，甚效。或用理阴煎加丁香以疏气，妙亦如之。　　凡以大病之后，或以虚羸之极，或以虚损误攻而致呃逆者，此最危之证。察其中虚，速宜补脾；察其阴虚，速宜补肾。如前二条固其法矣，然犹恐不及，则惟大补元煎及右归饮之类，斯其庶几者也。　　呃逆证，凡声强气盛而脉见滑实者，多宜清降；若声小息微而脉见微弱者，多宜温补。　　凡伤寒之呃，亦无非气逆之病，其有与杂证不同者，如仲景所言则其类也。然犹有未悉及治有未备者，谨略如左。　　伤寒胃中虚冷等证，大约与前杂证相似，悉宜如前以温中等剂治之。或如仲景所言胃中虚冷及饮水则哕等证，当以仲景法治之。　　伤寒邪在表者，与里无涉，故无哕证。[34p]

    The root of this nausea mainly lies in the kidneys; therefore, I formulate the Guiqi Decoction to address it, which is quite effective. Some use the Li Yin Decoction with added clove to disperse the qi, and it is also excellent.

    In cases following severe illness, or those who are extremely thin and weak, or who suffer from weakness due to overexertion leading to nausea, this is the most critical condition. If the deficiency within is noted, one should promptly nourish the spleen; if it is a deficiency of yin, one should promptly nourish the kidneys. The first two methods are indeed firm, yet if there is still concern, then one should resort to great tonifying formulas like the Yuan Decoction and the You Gui Decoction, which may be the best options.

    In cases of nausea, if the voice is strong and the energy is robust with a slippery and full pulse, one generally should clear it down; if the voice is small and the breath slight with a weak pulse, one generally should warm and tonify.

    For nausea due to exterior cold, it ultimately is another manifestation of qi counterflow, which may differ from mixed conditions, as mentioned by Zhang Zhongjing regarding its categories. However, if there are still things unclarified or treatments insufficient, I will briefly mention them as follows.

    In cases of cold in the stomach due to external cold, conditions are generally similar to the previous mixed conditions and should be treated as mentioned before with warming and middle-regulating remedies. If the stomach is cold and drinking water leads to nausea, then it should be treated according to Zhang Zhongjing’s methods. If the pathogen resides in the exterior, it has no relation to the interior, thus there is no nausea.[34p]

    惟少阳证邪在半表半里之间，则寒热往来气为邪抑而哕逆者，有之矣，宜柴陈煎主之。有寒者加丁香，有火者加黄芩，或小柴胡汤亦可。　　伤寒失下，邪入正阳明，内热之极，三焦干涸，阴道不行，而上冲作呃者，必宜去火去闭，斯逆气得降而哕乃可愈。然必察邪之微甚：如无坚实胀满等证，而但以干涸燥热者，宜白虎汤，或竹叶石膏汤，或泻心汤凉解之；若果有燥粪大便闭结，胀满实坚俱全者，宜三承气汤下之。　　伤寒邪有未解，而用温补太过者，则其中焦气逆，最能为哕，惟安胃饮为最妙。若气逆无火者，宜橘皮汤；若兼表邪未解者，宜柴陈煎。　　伤寒误攻，或吐或下，或误用寒凉，以致脾肾胃气大虚大寒而发哕者，大为危候，速当以前杂证温胃理阴等法调治之，恐迟则无济于事也。　　按张子和吐法，亦可治哕者，以其气得伸而郁则散也。故凡气实而郁者，在子和之法，亦所宜用。[35p]

    If the evil of lesser yang is located between the half exterior and half interior, resulting in alternating chills and fever along with qi being hindered leading to hiccups, it can be treated with Chai-Chen decoction. If accompanied by cold, add cloves; if with heat, add Huangqin; or Xiao-Chai-Hu decoction may also be appropriate.

    In cases of cold damage causing downward obstruction, if the evil enters the upright yangming and internal heat reaches its extreme, with the three burners dried up, the vaginal discharge ceased, and hiccups arising due to upward qi rebellion, it is essential to clear the heat and remove the obstruction, so that the rebellious qi can descend and thus alleviate the hiccups. However, it is crucial to carefully assess the severity of the evil: if there are no solid distension symptoms, only dryness and heat, then Bai-Hu decoction or Zhu-ye-Shi-Gao decoction, or Xie-Xin decoction to cool and resolve should be used; if there is indeed dry feces constipation and solid distension, then San-Cheng-Qi decoction should be administered.

    In cases of cold damage where the evil has not yet dispersed, using too much warming and tonifying treatments can cause the middle burner qi to rebel, which can especially lead to hiccups; in such cases, Anwei drink is the best remedy. If there is rebellious qi without fire, then use Ju-Pi decoction; if there is simultaneous exterior evil unresolved, then Chai-Chen decoction is appropriate.

    In situations where cold damage is mistakenly attacked, whether by vomiting, purging, or wrongly using cold cooling methods, leading to severe deficiency and cold of the spleen, kidneys, and stomach, which causes hiccups, it becomes a critical condition. Immediate adjustment using methods that warm the stomach and regulate yin is needed, for delay may render the situation irreparable.

    Observing Zhang Zihe's method of vomiting can also treat hiccups, as it can allow the qi to extend and disperse when it is stagnant. Therefore, for cases of fullness and stagnation, Zhang Zihe's method is indeed applicable.[35p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　论治法

    　　扬治者，乃气沉而不能上也。气得扬而展舒，倘沉抑不扬，则必有呃逆之证，必用药以扬之，则气舒展也。方用当归、白芍、黄芪、白朮各三钱，熟地五钱，人参、茯苓、川芎各一钱，柴胡、升麻各五分，水煎服。此八珍汤也，妙是血气平补，若用甘草而不用黄芪，则不是八珍汤矣。气血平补既无偏曲，而后以升麻、柴胡扬之，使血气流动，自无血并气而成呃逆之证矣。设止补其阳而不补其阴，则阳旺而阴愈消；设止补其阴而不补其阳，则阴旺而阳愈息。[36p]

    Secret Method of the Stone Chamber
    By Chen Shiduo, Qing Dynasty

    Discussion on Treatment Method

    When the qi is disturbed and cannot rise, it is in a state of stagnation. If the qi can rise and spread freely, but is instead suppressed and unable to ascend, there will inevitably be signs of rebellious qi, requiring the use of medicine to promote its upward movement, allowing the qi to spread and expand.

    The prescription includes three qian each of Dang Gui, Bai Shao, Huang Qi, and Bai Zhu, five qian of Shu Di, and one qian each of Ren Shen, Fu Ling, and Chuan Xiong, along with five fen each of Chai Hu and Sheng Ma, to be decocted in water for consumption. This is the Eight Treasure Decoction, effective for balancing blood and qi. If licorice is used instead of Huang Qi, it no longer qualifies as the Eight Treasure Decoction.

    Once the balance of qi and blood is achieved without any deviation, one can then use Sheng Ma and Chai Hu to help it rise, promoting the flow of blood and qi, thus eliminating any signs of rebellious qi. If only the yang is supplemented without the yin, the yang will flourish while the yin will decline; conversely, if only the yin is supplemented without the yang, the yin will prosper while the yang will diminish.[36p]

    故必兼补之，始为有益，不可与发散之一类而并观之也。　　水气凌心包之络，呃逆不止，死证也。而吾以为可救者，心包为水气所凌，惟恐犯心，所以呃逆不止者，欲号召五脏之气，共救水气之犯心也。水气凌心包，以成呃逆之证，亦止须分消其水湿之气，而呃逆自除也。　　方用止呃汤，茯苓、薏仁各一两，苍朮、白朮、人参各三钱，芡实五钱，半夏、陈皮各一钱，丁香五分，吴茱萸三分，水煎服。－剂而呃即止，二剂而呃即愈。此方健胃固脾，虽利湿分水而不消真气，故能补心包而壮心君之位，不必治呃而呃自定矣。
    　　　　方

    　　小承气汤 【仲景，下同】 　治大便不通，哕数讝语者。　　大黄四两　厚朴三两，炙　枳实大者三枚，炙　　右三味，以水四升煮取一升二合，去滓分温二服，得利则止。[37p]

    Therefore, it is necessary to supplement it comprehensively. Initially, this is beneficial, and it should not be viewed alongside the dispersed kinds. When water qi overwhelms the heart protector's network, there is persistent belching, which is a sign of impending death. However, I believe it can be salvaged because the heart protector is overwhelmed by water qi, and there is concern about the heart being harmed. Therefore, persistent belching occurs because it seeks to summon the qi of the five organs to jointly rescue the heart threatened by water qi. As water qi overwhelms the heart protector, leading to belching symptoms, it is essential to merely disperse the dampness of water qi, and the belching will cease naturally.

    To stop belching, use the following decoction: one tael each of Poria and Job's tears; three qian each of Atractylodes, White Atractylodes, and Ginseng; five qian of Foxnut; one qian each of Pinellia and dried tangerine peel; five fen of Clove; and three fen of the fruit of Evodia. Boil in water and take the decoction. After one dose, belching will stop; after two doses, it will be cured. This formula strengthens the stomach and solidifies the spleen. Although it promotes the excretion of dampness and water, it does not deplete true qi; thus, it can supplement the heart protector and strengthen the position of the heart ruler without needing to treat belching—belching will resolve itself.

    Formula:

    Small Chengqi Decoction [Zhongjing, same below] is used to treat constipation and frequent belching with incoherent speech. Use four ounces of Rhubarb, three ounces of Magnolia Bark, and three pieces of roasted bitter orange (large). Combine the three ingredients and simmer with four liters of water until one liter and two portions remain. Strain and divide into two warm doses; cease once benefits are obtained.[37p]

    Xiao Banxia Decoction treats jaundice and vomiting.
    Banxia (1 sheng), fresh ginger (0.5 jin).
    Combine these two ingredients with 7 sheng of water, boil down to 1.5 sheng, and divide into warm doses for repeated consumption.

    Qianghuo and Fuzi Powder treats post-vomiting diarrhea, cold stomach, and reverse coughing.
    Qianghuo (remove the root), Fuzi (prepared and remove skin and navel), and fennel (fried), each 0.5 liang;
    dried ginger (prepared and remove soil), and clove, each 1 liang.
    Grind them into a fine powder. Each dose is 2 liang, mix with 1 cup of water, add a pinch of salt, and simmer until reduced to 0.7 cups. Take it warm on an empty stomach. Danxi does not use cloves but substitutes with wood fragrance.

    Tangerine Peel Decoction treats post-vomiting diarrhea, stomach weakness, and upper heat causing reverse coughing.
    Tangerine peel (remove the white) (2 liang), ginseng, and licorice (processed), each 0.5 liang.
    Grind finely. Each dose is 4 qian, with 1.5 cups of water, a small piece of bamboo leaf, 5 slices of fresh ginger, and 2 dates. Boil until reduced to 0.7 cups, strain, and take warm at any time.

    Persimmon Calyx Decoction treats chest fullness and persistent reverse coughing.
    Persimmon calyx and clove, each 1 liang.
    Chew these ingredients. Each dose is 4 qian, with 1.5 cups of water, 5 slices of ginger, and boil until reduced to 0.7 cups. Strain and take warm at any time.

    Use 5 qian from this blend, simmer in water for consumption.[38p]

    Xi Xian San: Treats phlegm and sticky throat, for persistent coughing.

    • 14 pieces of Banxia, one piece of pig's tooth soapberry, roasted.
    • Half a cup of water, five slices of ginger, decoct to seven parts, drink warm.
    • For those unable to drink, administer by injection; shortly thereafter, induce vomiting.

    Qing Bai San: For incessant coughing.

    • Equal parts of Qingdai, white alum, and roasted Wu Mei pulp.
    • Grind into powder, take two qian per dose; mix with licorice soup to ingest.
    • First drink a cup of licorice soup, then take the medicine to induce vomiting.

    Ren Shen Lu Tang: Used for weak persons with cough and phlegm.

    • Three qian of ginseng and reed, one cup of water; decoct to five or seven boils, drink warm to induce vomiting.

    Shi Yan Tang: Treats cough and all phlegm conditions; especially effective when used in emergencies.

    • One liang of table salt, wrapped in damp paper and roasted until red; remove and place in two bowls of river water.
    • In a clay pot, roast the salt, decoct to five or seven boils, let cool slightly, and drink to induce vomiting.

    Xian Chen Tang: Treats hiccups and a near-death condition.

    • Five qian of Banxia and two and a half qian of fresh ginger, grated; this is one dose, decoct in water to consume.

    Wen Zhong San: Treats vomiting and diarrhea, and for coldness in the stomach after illness; cough with three to four sporadic sounds, or several sounds connected; difficult to treat if breath does not return.

    • One qian each of clove, persimmon calyx, ginseng, Poria, tangerine peel, galangal, and Banxia; one and a half qian of fresh ginger and three fen of licorice.
    • Grind into powder, this is one dose, decoct in water to consume.[42p]

    　　温病热哕：乃伏热在胃，令人胸满则气逆，逆则哕；或大下，胃中虚冷，亦令致此。茅根切、葛根切各半斤，水三升，煎一升半，每温服一盏，哕止即停。【庞安常方】
    　　虚寒呕哕，饮食不下：细辛去叶半两，丁香二钱半为末，每服一钱，柿蒂汤下。[45p]

    Wen Wei Drink: Treats cold in the stomach causing hiccups. Use 1-3 qian of ginseng or 1 liang, 1-2 qian of fried white atractylodes, 1-2 qian of fried and scorched dried ginger, 1-3 qian of dried tangerine peel, 1 qian of honey-fried licorice, and 1-2 qian of angelica.     Zuo Guan Decoction: Treats spleen damage from cold causing hiccups. Use 1 qian each of fried magnolia bark and fried dried tangerine peel, 7 fen of honey-fried licorice, and 1-2 qian each of cinnamon and dried ginger. Also include 2 qian each of fried yam, fried flat beans, pig's poria, and alisma. Combine with 1.5 zhongs of water and brew.

    Gui Qi Drink: Treats qi counterflow, hiccups, and vomiting, or symptoms related to cold affecting the spleen and kidneys. Use 3-5 qian of cooked rehmannia, 2 qian each of poria and flat beans, 1 qian each of cannon-fried dried ginger, cloves, and dried tangerine peel, and 1.5 qian of patchouli, along with 8 fen of honey-fried licorice. Combine with 1.5 zhongs of water, boil down to 7 parts, and take warm away from meals.

    Single Formulas

    Wen Bing Heat Hiccups: This arises from lurking heat in the stomach, causing chest fullness and counterflow of qi, leading to hiccups. Use half a jin each of sliced reed root and sliced kudzu, add 3 sheng of water, and boil down to 1.5 sheng. Take one cup warm until hiccups stop. [Pang Anchang's formula]

    Xu Han Vomiting and Hiccups, Inability to Eat: Use 5 fen of dried asarum without leaves and 2.5 qian of cloves, ground into powder. Take 1 qian with persimmon stem decoction.[45p]

    　　呕哕不止厥逆者，芦根三斤切，水煮浓汁频饮二升，必效，若以童子小便煮服，不过三升愈。【《肘后方》】　　又方：酢和面作弹丸二三十枚，以沸汤煮熟漉出，投浆水中，待温，吞三两枚。哕定即不用再吞，未定至晚再吞。【《兵部手集》】
    　　心痞呕哕，心下痞坚：生姜八两，水三升，煮一升，半夏五合洗，水五升煮一升，取汁同煮一升半，分再服。【《千金》】
    　　温病发哕，因饮水多者：枇杷叶去毛炙，香茅根各半斤，水四升，煎二升，稍稍饮之。【庞安常方】
    　　肾气上哕：肾气自腹中起上筑于咽喉，逆气连属而不能吐，或至数十声，上下不得喘息，此由寒伤胃脘，肾虚气逆，上乘于胃，与气相并。《难经》谓之哕，《素问》云病深者其声哕，宜服此方；如不止，灸期门、关元、肾俞穴。用吴茱萸酢炒热，橘皮、附子去皮各一两为末，面糊丸梧子大，每姜汤下七十九。【《仁存方》】[46p]

    For persistent vomiting and belching: take three pounds of reed root, chop it, and boil it in water to create a concentrated juice. Drink two quarts of this frequently; it will definitely be effective. Alternatively, if prepared with the urine of a young boy and boiled, three quarts will suffice for recovery.

    Another remedy: mix vinegar with flour to make twenty to thirty small pills. Cook them in boiling water, then strain and place them in cold water until warm; swallow two or three pills. If the vomiting stops, there’s no need to take more; if it continues, take more in the evening.

    For a feeling of fullness in the heart accompanied by vomiting, with a firm mass below the heart: take eight taels of ginger, three quarts of water, and boil down to one quart. Take five handfuls of pinellia, wash it, then boil five quarts of water down to one quart. Combine this juice with the ginger broth to make one and a half quarts, and divide to take in portions.

    For vomiting due to warm illness from excessive drinking: use half a pound each of loquat leaves (after removing the hairs) and lemon grass root, boil in four quarts of water to produce two quarts, and drink a little.

    For kidney qi causing belching: kidney qi rises from the abdomen to the throat, where the reverse qi connects but cannot be expelled, leading to many sounds of belching without relief. This occurs due to cold injuring the stomach, with kidney deficiency and qi reversal rising to the stomach. This is referred to as "belching" in the "Nanjing," and the "Suwen" states that for deep illness with this sound, this remedy should be taken. If it does not stop, moxibustion should be applied to the Qimen, Guanyuan, and Shenshu points. Use five-spice pepper (wu zhu yu) fried with vinegar, and mix one tael each of orange peel and processed aconite, grind into fine powder, and form into pills the size of a walnut; take with ginger decoction seven to nine times.[46p]

    　　哕逆不止：石莲肉六枚炒赤黄色，研末，冷熟水各半盏，和服便止。 【《图经》】
    　　治欬逆不止：用柿蒂十五枚，白盐梅半个，水一盏煎六分，不拘时温服。 【《医统》，下同】
    　　寒(食戹)呕哕：用吴茱萸泡过，青橘皮去白各二钱，水一盏，姜三片，煎七分服。　　又方：用川椒末，面糊丸梧桐子大，每服二十丸，白汤送下。　　又方：用陈皮、枳壳各二钱煎服。

    　　齅法：治咳逆服药不效者，用硫黄、乳香等分，以酒煎，令患人以鼻齅之效。一方用雄黄一味，煎酒齅。
