    　　　　针灸

    　　《灵枢经》曰：黄帝曰：人之哕者，何气使然？岐伯曰：谷入于胃，胃气上注于肺。今有故寒气与新谷气，俱还入于胃，新故相乱，真邪相攻，气并相逆，复出于胃，故为哕。补手太阴，泻足少阴。　　肺主为哕，取手太阴、足少阴。[47p]

    Here is the translated text:

    Persistent belching: Fry six pieces of stone lotus meat until they turn reddish-yellow, grind into a powder, mix with half a cup of cold cooked water, and take to stop it.

    For treating unceasing coughing and belching: Use fifteen pieces of persimmon stems, half a piece of white salt plum, and one cup of water, decocting to six parts, and take warm at any time.

    For cold-induced vomiting: Use two qian of wuzhuyu soaked, and two qian each of the white part of green tangerine peel. Add one cup of water and three slices of ginger, decoct to seven parts to take. Another prescription: Use powdered Sichuan pepper to make pills the size of wutong seeds, taking twenty pills each time with white broth. Another prescription: Use two qian each of dried tangerine peel and bitter orange to decoct and take.

    Method to treat stubborn cough when medication is ineffective: Use equal parts of sulfur and frankincense, decocted in wine for the patient to inhale. Another method involves using realgar alone, decocted in wine for inhalation.

    For chronic cough with repeated coughs of one or two dozen times: Take half a cup of ginger juice, one spoonful of honey, decoct until hot, and take warm. Effective after three doses.

    Acupuncture

    The "Spiritual Pivot" states: The Yellow Emperor asked: What qi causes belching in a person? Qibo replied: Food enters the stomach, and the stomach qi rises to the lungs. Now, if cold qi and new grain qi both enter the stomach together, they disturb each other, the true and the evil qi attack each other, and the qi reverses and exits the stomach, thus causing belching. Strengthen the hand taiyin and drain the foot shaoyin. The lung is responsible for belching; therefore, treat with hand taiyin and foot shaoyin.[47p]

    　　《甲乙经》曰：烦心，客寒热，善哕，劳宫主之。　　脾逆气寒，厥急烦心，善唾哕噫，胸满激呼，胃气上逆心痛，太渊主之。　　《千金方》曰：少海，主气逆呼吸，噫哕呕。　　温留，主伤寒寒热，头痛哕衄，肩不举。　　又方：灸承浆七壮，炷如麦大。
    　　又方：灸脐下四指七壮。
    　　胃中热病善哕，灸三里三十壮，穴在膝下三寸。　　《济生方》曰：灸欬逆，其法：妇人屈乳头向下尽处骨间是穴，丈夫及乳小者，以一指为率正，男左女右，与乳相直间陷中动脉处是穴，艾炷如小豆许，灸三壮。　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：一切呃逆不止，男左女右，乳下黑尽处一韭叶许，灸三壮；病甚者，灸二七壮。　　《古今医统》曰：呃逆，灸膻中、中脘、气海、三里。　　《医学纲目》日，气逆发呃，取膻中、中脘，先补后泻；不已，再取三里、肺俞、行间。　　噫呃服药无效，灸期门必愈。[48p]

    The "Jia Yi Jing" states: Mental distress, cold and heat in the guest, frequent hiccups, and strains the Heart of the Palace. When the Spleen rebels with cold Qi, causing urgent mental distress, frequent spitting of phlegm, chest fullness with loud exhalations, and gastric Qi reversing leading to heart pain, it is governed by Taiyuan.

    The "Qian Jin Fang" states: Shaohai governs reversed Qi during breathing, belching, and vomiting. Wenliu governs cold and heat injuries, headache with hiccups and nosebleeds, and inability to lift the shoulders.

    Another method: Moxibustion on Chengjiang, seven times with moxa the size of wheat grains.

    Another method: Moxibustion four finger widths below the navel, seven times.

    For heat disorders in the stomach with frequent hiccups, moxibustion on Sanli, thirty times; the point is three inches below the knee.

    The "Ji Sheng Fang" states: For hiccups and reversal, the method is: for women, press the nipple downward to the bone's end, which is the point; for men or women with small breasts, take one finger's width as a reference, men on the left, women on the right, the point is between the breasts near the pulsating artery, moxa the size of a small bean, three times.

    The "Wei Sheng Bao Jian" states: For all persistent hiccups, men on the left, women on the right, at the dark point beneath the breast, about the size of a chive leaf, moxa three times; for severe cases, moxa twenty-one times.

    The "Gu Jin Yi Tong" states: Hiccups, moxa at Shanzhong, Zhongwan, Qihai, and Sanli.

    The "Yi Xue Gang Mu" states: When Qi reverses and causes hiccups, target Shanzhong and Zhongwan first to tonify and then to drain; if ineffective, additionally target Sanli, Feiyu, and Xingjian.

    If hiccups do not respond to medication, moxibustion at Qimen will certainly cure it.[48p]

    　　　　医案

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：一妇人头重壮热，面红，寒热往来，干呕咳逆，胸胁痛，不能转侧，耳鸣，食不下，先以涌泻，复服益元散加青黛、薄荷末调二三服，前证俱减。戴人诊之曰：此病常欲痛哭为快。妇曰：然。常有此，不知何谓。戴人曰：少阳相火凌烁肺金，金受火制，屈无所告，肺主悲，故欲痛哭而为快也。再加归芍黄连解毒汤数剂全瘥。
    　　《丹溪心法》曰：一女子年踰笄，性躁味厚。暑月因大怒而咳逆发，举身跳动，脉不可诊，神昏，视其形气俱实。曰：膈上有痰，怒气连郁，痰热相搏，气不得降，非吐不可。以人参芦煎饮，大吐顽痰数碗，昏睡一日而安。人参入手太阴，补阴中之阳者也；芦则反是，大泻太阴之阳。女子暴怒气上，肝主怒，肺主气，怒则气逆，肝木乘火侮肺，故咳逆而神昏。参芦善吐，今痰尽气降火息，金气复位，胃气得和而解。[49p]

    Medical Case Report

    The "Rumen Shiqin" states: A woman presented with a heavy head and strong heat, a flushed face, alternating chills and fevers, dry heaving and coughing, pain in the chest and ribs, difficulty turning over, tinnitus, and loss of appetite. Initially, a purgative was administered, followed by a modified Yiyuan San with Qingdai and mint powder in two to three doses, resulting in reduced symptoms. A physician diagnosed that this illness often makes one want to cry to feel relief. The woman confirmed this, stating it happens frequently but she did not understand why. The physician explained that the Shaoyang fire was attacking the Lung metal, which was weakened by the fire, causing a lack of expression. Since the Lung governs sorrow, this led to the urge to cry for relief. Adding Guizhao Huanglian Jiedu Decoction in several doses resulted in complete recovery.

    The "Danxi Xinfah" states: A girl beyond the age of marriage had a disposition of restlessness and likened rich tastes. During the hot months, she became extremely angry, leading to coughing and a convulsive body, with a pulse that was difficult to diagnose, and she appeared dazed with both her form and energy being substantial. It was determined that phlegm was present above the diaphragm, anger was repressed, and the heat from phlegm clashed, obstructing the qi from descending, making vomiting necessary. A decoction of ginseng and reed was prescribed, resulting in a significant expulsion of stubborn phlegm through several bowls and a day of deep sleep thereafter. Ginseng enters the Taiyin channel, replenishing the Yang within the Yin; whereas reed does the opposite, strongly draining the Yang of Taiyin. The girl's violent anger raised her qi; the Liver governs anger, the Lung governs qi, and with anger, the qi rebels. The wooden Liver overcomes the Lung's metal, leading to coughing and confusion. The combination of ginseng and reed effectively promotes vomiting, resolving phlegm and allowing the qi to descend, extinguishing the fire, restoring the metal qi, and harmonizing the stomach qi, bringing relief.[49p]

    　　赵立通年近五十，质弱而多怒。七月炎暑，大饥索饭于家，不能急具，因大怒，两日后得滞下病，口渴。自以冷水调生蜜饮之甚快，滞下亦渐缓。如此五七日，召予。视脉稍大不数，遂令止蜜水，渴时且令以人参、白朮煎汤调益元散与之，滞下亦渐收。七八日后觉倦甚发呃。予知其因下久而阴虚也，令其守前药，然滞下尚未止，又以炼蜜饮之，如此者三日，呃犹未止。众皆尤药之未当，将以姜附饮之。予曰：补药无速效，附子非补阴者，服之必死。众曰：冷水饮多，得无寒乎？予曰：炎暑如此，饮凉非寒，勿多疑。待以数日，药力到，当自止。又四日而呃止，滞下亦安。[50p]

    Zhao Litong, nearing fifty, was of weak constitution and often angry. In July, during a scorching heat, he suffered from severe hunger while requesting food at home, but as it couldn't be prepared quickly, he became very angry. Two days later, he developed retention issues and experienced thirst. He believed that mixing cold water with honey would quench his thirst quickly, and his retention gradually eased. After five to seven days, he summoned me. Upon checking, his pulse was slightly strong but not rapid, so I instructed him to stop the honey water. When thirsty, he was to take a decoction of ginseng and white atractylodes mixed with Yiyuan powder, and the retention continued to gradually improve. A week later, he felt very fatigued and began to burp. I recognized this was due to his prolonged retention leading to kidney deficiency, so I advised him to stick with the previous medication. However, the retention had not stopped yet, and he continued with the honey drink. After three days of this, the burping had not ceased. Others believed that the medicine was inappropriate and intended to add ginger to the drink. I said: “Tonifying medicines do not produce immediate effects, and aconite does not tonify the kidneys; taking it would surely be fatal.” They asked: “Could it be because of drinking too much cold water, leading to coldness?” I replied: “Under such sultry heat, drinking something cool is not cold; don’t doubt this too much. Wait a few days; the medicinal properties will take effect, and it will resolve itself.” Four days later, the burping stopped, and the retention was also stable.[50p]

    　　陈择仁年近七十，厚味之人也，有久嗽病而作止不常。新秋患滞下，食大减，至五七日后呃作。召予视之，脉皆大豁，众以为难。予曰：形瘦者尚可为。以人参、白朮汤下大补丸以补血，至七日而安。
    　　超越陈氏二十余岁，因饱后奔走数里，遂患哕病，但食物则连哕百余声，半日不止，饮酒与汤则不作，至晚发热，如此者二月，脉濇数，以血入气中治之，用桃仁承气汤加红花煎服，下污血数次即减。再用木香和中丸，加丁香服之，十日而愈。[51p]

    Chen Zerens was nearly seventy years old, a person with a robust appetite, but he had a chronic cough that disturbed him intermittently. In the early autumn, he suffered from stagnation and reduced his food intake, leading to belching after five or seven days. He summoned me to examine him; his pulse was forceful and wide, which others deemed serious. I said, "Those who are thin can still be treated." I prescribed a large tonic pill made with ginseng and white atractylodes to replenish his blood, and after seven days, he was stable.

    Zhou Yue, who was over twenty years younger than Chen, developed a belching condition after running several miles following a heavy meal. He belched over a hundred times without stopping for half a day; drinking alcohol and soup did not trigger any belching. By evening, he developed a fever, and this lasted for two months. His pulse was thin and weak, so I treated him by nourishing the blood and pushing it into the qi using a modified Tao Ren Chengqi Decoction, which helped him discharge dark blood numerous times and alleviate his symptoms. Then, I used a Qi-regulating pill with muskmallow, and combined it with clove. After ten days, he recovered.[51p]

    　　洪孺人年二十六岁，夏月因事为长上所阻，怒气郁抑不得舒，须臾就浴，汤热不可近，怒气复增，就闷绝昏倒，乃以衣遮掩就房，须臾咳逆大作，每一声，必浑身为跳跃，仍复昏闷，凡三五息一作，脉不可诊。予曰：此膈上有痰逆为怒气所郁，痰热相搏，气不得降而逆，非吐则不可。是时夜半，又事出仓卒，适有人参芦二两在彼，浓煎饮之，大吐稠痰二升许，通体得汗，困睡半夜而安。
    　　《医学正传》曰：东阳李氏子病伤寒阳明内实，医与补药治而成发呃。十日后，召予诊其脉，长而实大，与大承气汤大下之，热退而呃亦止。
    　　盘松周氏子得伤寒证，七日热退而呃，连声不绝，举家仿徨。召予诊脉，六脉皆沉细无力，人倦甚。以补中益气汤作大剂，加炮附子一钱，一日三贴，兼舆灸乳根、气海三处，当日呃止，脉亦充而平安。[52p]

    At the age of twenty-six, Lady Hong was obstructed by her superiors due to matters in the summer months. She harbored pent-up anger that could not be released. Soon after, she bathed in water that was too hot to approach, which exacerbated her anger, causing her to feel faint and collapse. She covered herself with her clothes and went to her room. Shortly after, she began to cough violently; each cough made her body jolt, leading to further dizziness. This occurred every three to five breaths, and her pulse could not be diagnosed. I said: "There is phlegm in the upper part of the body, and the anger has caused it to be stagnant. The hot phlegm is clashing, preventing qi from descending, so it must be expelled." At that time, it was midnight, and suddenly, someone happened to have two taels of ginseng and reed available. A concentrated decoction was made, resulting in her expelling about two sheng of thick phlegm, sweating profusely, and after half the night of being exhausted, she found peace.

    In "The Correct Transmission of Medicine," it states: The son of the Li family from Dongyang suffered from a yangming interior excess due to febrile disease. The physician treated him with tonic herbs, leading to a paroxysm of vomiting. Ten days later, he called me to diagnose his pulse, which was long, strong, and big. I administered the Da Chengqi Decoction to purge him significantly; the fever subsided and his vomiting also ceased.

    The son of the Zhou family from Pansong presented with symptoms of febrile disease. After seven days, the fever subsided but he continued to vomit repeatedly, causing distress to the family. They summoned me to diagnose his pulse, which showed all six pulses were deep, thin, and weak, and he was very fatigued. I prescribed a large dose of the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, adding one qian of fried Fuzi, with three doses a day, along with moxibustion on three points: Rugen and Qihai. That same day, his vomiting ceased, and his pulse became fuller and stable.[52p]

    　　《医学准绳六要》曰：一老人内伤饮食，消导未减，一人误与润肠丸二服，下清水，胀痛转甚；一人复投巴豆丸二服，致咳逆不止。用大剂六君子汤二贴至五贴全止，补养而愈。
    　　《医学纲目》曰：予长兄九月得滞下，每夜五十余行，呕逆食不下，五六日后加呃逆。与丁香一粒噙之立止，但少时又至。遂用黄连泻心汤加竹茹饮之，呃虽少止，滞下未安。如此者十余日，遂空心用御米壳些少濇其滑，日间用白朮、陈皮之类补其虚。自服御米壳之后，呃声渐轻，滞下亦收而安。
    　　有病伤寒将愈，忽患呃逆，予与古人治呃逆之药殆遍，皆不愈。计出无奈，遂用皂角末吹入鼻中，得嚏而呃逆止；少时又呃，又与皂角末，嚏而止者，凡数百次。其嚏时出痰涕渐多，自是呃逆渐疏，至二三日而止。此是合经草刺鼻嚏之法，故书之。[53p]

    The "Six Essentials of Medical Principles" states: A senior experienced internal injuries from diet, and although digestion had not decreased, one person mistakenly took two doses of a laxative pill, leading to worsening abdominal distension and pain; another person took two doses of a purgative, resulting in incessant coughing. They were treated with large doses of the Six Gentlemen Decoction, up to five applications, and through tonification, recovered.

    The "Medical Compendium" mentions: My elder brother had recurring diarrhea for nine months, with over fifty bowel movements each night, vomiting food, and after five or six days became increasingly nauseous. I gave him a grain of clove to dissolve, which immediately stopped the nausea, but after a while, it returned. Therefore, I used the Huang Lian Xie Xin Decoction with added bamboo shavings to drink; although nausea lessened, the diarrhea remained unresolved. This persisted for over ten days, and so I used a small amount of polished rice husks to help absorb the excess fluid and during the day, I supplemented with white atractylodes and dried tangerine peel to nourish his deficiency. After taking the polished rice husks, the nausea gradually subsided, and the diarrhea also stabilized.

    There was a patient recovering from a cold who suddenly developed nausea. I tried nearly all remedies for nausea known to ancient practitioners, but none worked. Out of desperation, I used powdered soap pod to blow into the nose, leading to a sneeze that stopped the nausea; however, it returned after a while, so I repeated the use of powdered soap pod, resulting in multiple sneezes that alleviated it for hundreds of times. Each sneeze led to increasing phlegm and mucus, which gradually cleared the nausea, and within two to three days, it stopped. This is a method that aligns with the principles of acupuncture and nasal sneezing, thus I record it here.[53p]

    　　　噫气门

    　　　　黄帝素问

    　　　　　诊要经终论

    　　太阴终者，腹胀闭不得息，善噫善呕。　　 【注　足太阴脉入腹属脾，故为腹胀。手太阴脉上膈属肺而主呼吸，故为不得息。胀满则升降难，不得息则气道滞，故为噫为呕。】
    　　　　　痹论

    　　心痹者脉不通，烦则心下鼓，暴上气而喘，嗌干善噫。　　 【注　邪薄心下，鼓动而上干心脏则烦，故烦则心下鼓也。逆气暴上，则喘而嗌干。心主噫，心气上逆而出，则善噫也。】
    　　　　　脉解篇

    　　太阴所谓上走心为噫者，阴盛而上走于阳明，阳明络属心，故曰上走心为噫也。　　 【注　噫者嗳气也，太阴之气，从阳明而上出于心，则为噫也。】
    　　　　　刺禁论

    　　刺中心一日死，其动为噫。
    　　 【注　心在气为噫，噫则心气绝矣。】
    　　　　灵枢经

    　　　　　经脉篇[54p]

    Yiqimen (The Door of Breath)

    Huangdi Suwen (The Yellow Emperor's Simple Questions)

    Essentials of Diagnosis and Final Discussion

    The Taiyin condition manifests as abdominal distention, leading to difficulty in breathing, along with frequent belching and vomiting. 【Note: The foot Taiyin channel enters the abdomen corresponding to the spleen, thus causing abdominal distention. The hand Taiyin channel affects the diaphragm and is related to the lungs, hence the difficulty in breathing. When distention occurs, elevation and descent are challenging; when breathing is restricted, qi pathways are obstructed, resulting in belching and vomiting.】

    Discussion on Obstruction

    In the case of heart obstruction, the pulse does not flow smoothly, causing agitation that leads to a sensation of fullness below the heart, sudden upward rising qi, and dry throat with frequent belching. 【Note: When pathogenic factors obscure below the heart, it stirs and affects the heart, causing agitation; hence, agitation leads to fullness below the heart. Reversed qi suddenly rises, resulting in wheezing and a dry throat. The heart governs belching, and when heart qi reverses and exits, it leads to frequent belching.】

    Pulse Explanation Chapter

    The Taiyin condition, which is said to ascend to the heart as belching, arises from the abundance of yin that ascends to Yangming; since Yangming is linked to the heart, it is thus called ascending to the heart as belching. 【Note: Belching refers to the expulsion of qi. The qi of Taiyin ascends from Yangming and exits through the heart, resulting in belching.】

    Discussion on Needle Prohibition

    Needling the center of the heart leads to death in one day, causing a reaction of belching. 【Note: When the heart is obstructed, it leads to belching; thus, if belching occurs, heart qi is exhausted.】

    Lingshu (The Spiritual Pivot)

    Channels and Vessels Chapter[54p]

    　　脾足太阴之脉，是，动则病舌本强，食则呕，胃脘痛，腹胀善噫。　　 【注　脾是动则病气而及于经，从经而及于脏腑，故为舌本强呕痛胀诸证。善噫者，脾气上走心为噫。】
    　　　　　九针篇

    　　心主噫。
    　　 【注　噫者，中焦之逆气上走心也。】
    　　　　金匮要略 【汉　张机】

    　　　　　三焦竭证

    　　问曰：三焦竭部，上焦竭善噫，何谓也？师曰：上焦受中焦气，未和不能消谷，故能噫耳。下焦竭即遗溺失便，其气不和，不能自禁制，不须治，久则愈。
    　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　论证治

    　　嗳气，胃中有火有痰，不可服软石膏丸。本方痰条下云：噫气吞酸，此系食郁有热，火气冲上，黄芩为君，南星、半夏、陈皮为佐，热多加青黛。
    　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

    　　　　　病属痰火

    　　胃中郁火，膈上稠痰，饮食郁成，宜祛痰火也，润下丸、古萸连丸。
    　　　　　治分虚实[55p]

    The spleen's channel of the foot Taiyin manifests in several ways: when disturbed, it leads to a strong feeling in the root of the tongue, vomiting after eating, stomach pain, and abdominal bloating with frequent belching.

    Note: The spleen, when in motion, affects Qi, which then influences the channels and organs, resulting in symptoms like a strong tongue, vomiting, pain, and bloating. Frequent belching indicates that spleen Qi is rising towards the heart.

    The heart governs belching.

    Note: Belching is the reverse Qi of the middle burner rising to the heart.

    Regarding the symptoms of the Sanjiao (Triple Burner), the question arises: what does "exhaustion of the upper jiao" with belching mean? The master replies: the upper jiao receives Qi from the middle burner; if it is not harmonized, it cannot digest food, hence the belching. Exhaustion of the lower jiao results in loss of urine and stool, as Qi is unregulated and cannot be controlled. No treatment is necessary; it will resolve with time.

    In treating belching, if there is heat and phlegm in the stomach, one should not take soft gypsum pills. Regarding the prescription, it states that belching with sour regurgitation is due to food stagnation combined with heat; this is related to the rising fire Qi. Use Huangqin as the main ingredient, and add Nanshen, Banxia, and Chenpi as assistants; if there is more heat, add Qingdai.

    When phlegm-heat is present, with stagnant fire in the stomach and thick phlegm in the diaphragm due to dietary accumulation, it is necessary to expel phlegm-heat, using pills such as Runxia Wan and Guyu Lian Wan.

    Treatment should distinguish between deficiency and excess.[55p]

    　　气盛实嗳，食罢嗳转，腐气甚则物亦嗳转，多伤食湿热所致，二陈汤加苍朮、神曲、麦芽、姜炒黄连或保和丸。　　不因饮食常嗳者虚也，盖胃有浊气，膈有湿痰，俱能发嗳，六君子汤加沉香为君，厚朴、苏子为臣，吴萸为使；气逆匀气丸，或苏合香丸；甚者灵砂以镇坠之。
    　　　　医学正传 【明　虞抟】

    　　　　　总论

    　　《内经》曰：胃为水谷之海，无物不受，若夫湿面鱼腥生冷水果，以及烹飪调和粘滑难化等物，恣食无节，朝伤暮损而成清痰稠饮，滞于中宫，故为嘈杂嗳气，吞酸痞满，甚则为翻胃噎膈，即此之由也。夫嘈杂之为证也，似饥不饥，似痛不痛，而有懊憹不自宁之况者是也。其证或兼嗳气，或兼痞满，或兼恶心，渐至胃脘作痛，实痰火之为患也。治法以南星、半夏、橘红之类以消其痰，芩、连、栀子、石膏、知母之类以降其火，苍朮、白朮、芍药之类以健脾行湿，壮其本元。又当忌口节欲，无有不安者也。[56p]

    Excessive qi leads to belching, which increases after eating; when the rancid qi is strong, it can cause more belching. This is often due to the harmful effects of dampness and heat from food. For treatment, use Erchen Decoction with added Cangzhu, Shenqu, Malt, stir-fried Huanglian, or Baohe Pills. If persistent belching is not related to diet, it is due to deficiency, caused by stagnant turbid qi in the stomach and damp phlegm in the diaphragm, both of which can lead to belching. For this, administer Liu Junzi Decoction with Chenxiang as the chief ingredient, Houpu and Suzi as officials, and Wuyu as a messenger; also consider Qinigunqi Pill or Suhexiang Pill; for severe cases, Ling Sha can be used to settle the condition.

    General Discussion

    The "Neijing" states: The stomach is the sea of food and drink, receiving all substances. If one indulges without restraint in damp, fishy, cold, or overly slippery foods, it results in a build-up of thick phlegm, causing a noisy stomach and symptoms like acid reflux, fullness, and, in severe cases, vomiting and obstruction in the diaphragm. This manifests as a sensation of hunger without hunger, pain without pain, and a state of distress causing unease. Symptoms may include belching, fullness, nausea, leading to pain in the stomach area, indicative of phlegm-fire accumulation. Treatment should focus on herbs like Nansheng, Banxia, and Ju Hong to dispel phlegm; Qinjie, Lian, Zhizhi, Shigao, and Zhimai to reduce fire; and Cangzhu, Baizhu, and Shaoyao to strengthen the spleen and resolve dampness, thereby reinforcing the fundamental essence. Additionally, it is essential to avoid certain foods and practice moderation without disregarding personal discomfort.[56p]

    　　　　证治要诀 【明　戴思恭】

    　　　　　噫气吞酸

    　　噫气、吞酸、吐酸者，宿食所为，故曰中脘有饮则嘈，有宿食则酸，噫气吞酸，嗳宿腐气，逆咽酸水，亦有每晨吐清酸水数口，有日间无事者，亦有膈间常如酸折，皆饮食伤兼中脘虚所致，生料平胃散加神曲、麦蘗各半钱，或八味平胃散。
    　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

    　　　　　脾胃不和有痰有火

    　　丹溪曰：嗳气为胃中有痰有火。春甫谓嗳气多是胃气不和，窒塞不通，则嗳气，何以见之？凡人食饱后多有嗳气，由饮食饱则胃不舒畅而致然也。噫气若非食后，则为胃虚而不和。丹溪谓痰与火，特一端耳。
    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】[57p]

    Key Points on Diagnosis and Treatment

    Symptoms of Belching and Sourness

    Belching, swallowing sour air, and vomiting sour substance are caused by retained food. This is evidenced by symptoms in the middle abdomen: when there is fluid, it causes discomfort, and when there is retained food, it causes sourness. Belching and swallowing sour air, expelling rotten gas, and experiencing sour water reversing in the throat often manifest as spitting up clear sour water several times each morning. Some individuals may not experience this discomfort during the day, while others feel a consistent sour ache in the diaphragm. These issues are due to both the harm from food and a deficiency in the middle abdomen. The remedy is to use Pingwei Powder with equal parts shenqu and maiya, or alternatively, Bawei Pingwei Powder.

    Disharmony of Spleen and Stomach with Phlegm and Fire

    Danxi states that belching indicates the presence of phlegm and fire in the stomach. Chunfu believes that frequent belching is largely due to disharmony in the gastric qi, leading to blockage and discomfort. How can this be identified? Generally, after eating to fullness, people often expel gas since a full meal causes the stomach to feel uneasy. If belching occurs not long after meals, it suggests a deficiency in the stomach with resultant disharmony. While Danxi mentions phlegm and fire, it represents only one aspect of the condition.[57p]

    　　　　　总论

    　　《内经》所谓噫，即今所谓嗳气也。宣明五气论以心为噫，痹论以心痹者脉不通，烦则心下鼓，暴上气而喘，嗌干善噫。至真要大论以太阳司天，少阴之复，皆为哕噫。四时刺逆从论刺中心一日死，其动为噫。阴阳别论二阳一阴发病主惊骇，背痛，善噫，善欠，名曰风厥。脉解篇太阴所谓上走心为噫者，阴盛而上走于阳明，阳明络属心，故曰上走心为噫也。此乃噫从心出者也。厥阴在泉，腹胀善噫，得后于气则快然如衰。玉版论太阴终者善噫。《灵枢》云：足太阴是动，病腹胀善噫。又云：寒气客于胃，厥逆从下上散，复出于胃，故为噫。仲景谓上焦受中焦气未和不能消，是故能噫。又云：上焦不归者，噫而吞酸。不归者不至也。上焦之气不至其部，则物不能传化，故噫而吞酸。由是观之，噫者是火土之气，郁而不得发，故噫而出。王注解心为噫之义，象火炎上，烟随焰出，如痰闭膈间，中气不得伸而嗳者，亦土气内郁也。[58p]

    Summary

    The term "噫" in the "Inner Canon" corresponds to what is now called "aerophagia" or belching. The Five Qi Theory states that belching originates from the heart, while the theory of obstruction indicates that when the heart is blocked, the pulse does not flow smoothly, leading to sensations of fullness and labored breathing, accompanied by dryness in the throat and an inclination to belch. The "Great Treatise on True Principles" describes the role of the Taiyang in governing the heavens, while the recovery of the Shaoyin is associated with the occurrence of belching. The Four Seasons indicate that obstruction and counterflow treatment derived from piercing the center leads to death in one day and results in belching. The Yin-Yang Distinctions state that two Yangs and one Yin cause symptoms such as fright, back pain, a tendency to belch, and yawning; this is termed "wind syncope." The Pulse Interpretation chapter discusses how the Taiyin relates to the heart through belching, indicating that when Yin is abundant and ascends to the Yangming, and since Yangming connects to the heart, it is said that this ascent relates to belching. This indicates that belching emanates from the heart. The Jueyin in the pulse reflects abdominal bloating and belching, with relief from gas leading to a sensation of lightness. The discussion of the Taiyin concludes that prolonged conditions result in frequent belching. The "Spiritual Pivot" mentions the Foot Taiyin as active in conditions like abdominal bloating and belching. It also notes that cold qi lodges in the stomach, causing counterflow upwards that leads to belching. Zhang Zhongjing argues that if the upper jiao receives unbalanced qi from the middle jiao, it cannot digest properly, resulting in belching. Furthermore, if the qi of the upper jiao does not return, it can lead to belching and sour regurgitation, indicating that when the qi does not reach its respective areas, digestion is obstructed, resulting in belching and sourness. Thus, belching is viewed as the qi of fire and earth being constrained and unable to vent, leading to its outward expression. Wang’s commentary on the meaning of the heart relating to belching likens it to fire's ascent, with smoke following the flames; similarly, when phlegm obstructs the diaphragm, the central qi cannot extend, resulting in belching, which is also a manifestation of internal earth qi being stagnant.[58p]

    　　　　方

    　　槟榔散 【《千金方》，下同】 　治脾寒饮食不消，劳倦气胀噫满，忧恚不乐。　　槟榔八枚，皮子全　人参　茯苓　陈曲　厚仆　麦蘗　吴茱萸　白朮各二两　　右八味，治下筛，食后，酒服二方寸匕，日再。一方用橘皮一两半。　　又方　治腹胀善噫，食则欲呕，泄澼溏下，口干，四肢重，好怒，不欲闻人声，忘误，喉痹。　　黄连一两　禹余粮二两　白朮　干姜各三两　大麻子五两　桑白皮八两　大枣二十枚　　右七味(口父)咀，以水一斗二升，煮取三升，分四服。
    　　消食膏酒　治脾虚寒劳损，气胀噫满，食不下通，善噫。　　猪膏三升　宿姜　吴茱萸　白朮[59p]

    Recipe for Betel Nut Powder

    For treating cold spleen causing undigested food, fatigue, bloating, discomfort, and unhappiness:

    Take eight betel nuts, skin intact; two taels each of ginseng, poria, aged barley, thick-fleshed, wheat germ, evodia, and white atractylodes.

    Prepare these eight ingredients, sift them, and after meals, take two knife tips worth with wine, twice a day. In another recipe, use one and a half taels of tangerine peel.

    Additionally, for treating abdominal bloating, good belching, desire to vomit after eating, diarrhea, dry mouth, heavy limbs, irritability, aversion to human voices, forgetfulness, and throat dysfunction:

    Use one tael of coptis, two taels of yuyu grain, three taels each of white atractylodes and dried ginger, five taels of hemp seeds, eight taels of mulberry bark, and twenty jujubes.

    Crush these seven ingredients and boil with twelve liters of water until three liters remain, dividing into four doses.

    Digestive Syrup

    For treating spleen deficiency due to cold fatigue, bloating, discomfort, inability to eat, and good belching:

    Use three liters of pig fat, aged ginger, and evodia, along with white atractylodes.[59p]

    　　右四味，捣茱萸、白朮等二味，细细下筛为散，内姜汁膏中，煎取六升，温清酒一升，进方寸匕，日再。
    　　三台圆 【《济生方》】 　治五脏寒热积聚，胪胀肠鸣而噫，食不生肌肤，甚者呕逆。若伤寒疟已愈，令不复发。食饮后服五丸，多者十丸。常服令人大小便调和，长肌肉。　　茯苓半两　大黄　前胡各二两　硝石　葶苈　杏仁各一升　厚朴　附子　细辛　半夏各一两　　右十味为末，蜜和，捣五千杵，丸如梧子大，服五丸，稍加至十丸，以知为度。

    　　南星　半夏　软石膏　香附

    　　顺气木香散　治气不升降，胸膈痞闷，时或引痛；及酒食过伤，噫气吞酸，心脾刺痛，女人一切血气刺痛。　　砂仁　官桂　甘草炙　陈皮　厚朴　丁皮　茴香　桔梗　苍朮　木香　干姜　良姜　　右，水煎服。[60p]

    The four ingredients, consisting of Cornelian cherry and Tatarian aster among others, are to be ground and finely sifted into a powder. This is mixed into a syrup made from ginger juice, then boiled down to yield six sheng. One sheng of warm clear wine is added, and taken with a spoon twice daily.

    San Tai Yuan 【from Jisheng Fang】 is used to treat the accumulation of cold and heat in the five organs, leading to abdominal distension, bowel sounds, and sour belching, with food failing to nourish the skin; in severe cases, it can cause vomiting and reversal. If one has recovered from cold-induced fever and malaria, it prevents relapse. After meals, take five pills, increasing to ten if needed. Regular use harmonizes urination and defecation, promoting muscle growth.

    The ingredients are half a tael of Poria, two taels each of rhubarb and Peucedanum, one sheng each of saltpeter, agastache, and apricot kernels, along with one tael each of magnolia bark, aconite, asarum, and pinellia. These ten ingredients are ground to a powder, mixed with honey, and pounded 5,000 times to form pills the size of a walnut. Start by taking five pills, gradually increasing to ten as necessary.

    For belching, use the Danxi formula with the following: half a sheng of southern star, half a sheng of pinellia, soft gypsum, and cyperus; these can be made into pills or a decoction. This addresses the stagnant heat in the stomach and phlegm in the diaphragm.

    Shunqi Muxiang San treats conditions where qi fails to ascend or descend, causing chest congestion, occasional pain, and discomfort after overeating or drinking, which may lead to sour belching, heart and spleen pain, and menstrual pains in women. The ingredients include cardamom, cinnamon, roasted licorice, dried tangerine peel, magnolia bark, clove, fennel, platycodon, and Poria, along with dried and fresh ginger. These should be boiled and taken orally.[60p]

    　　异香散　治胃气不和，腹胁胀满，饮食难化，噫气吞酸，一切冷气结聚，腹中刺痛。　　莪朮炮　益智　甘草炙　三棱各六两　青皮　陈皮各三两　厚朴二两　石莲肉一两　　右銼，每服三钱，水煎，姜三片，枣一枚，入盐一捻，同煎服。

    Yixiang San - Treats disorders of the stomach, including disharmony of stomach qi, bloating in the abdomen and flanks, difficulty digesting food, acid regurgitation, accumulation of cold qi, and sharp pain in the abdomen.
    Ingredients: Six liang each of Echu, Poria, and Licorice (roasted), three liang each of Qiping and Chenpi, two liang of Houpo, and one liang of Shilianrou.
    Preparation: Ground together; each dose is three qian, decocted in water with three slices of ginger and one jujube, adding a pinch of salt, and taken.

    Toukekang - Treats disharmony of the spleen and stomach, stagnation of qi in the middle, fullness and heaviness in the chest, obstruction and difficulty in swallowing, acid regurgitation, sharp pain in the ribs, and vomiting of phlegm.
    Ingredients: One qian each of Muxiang, Bai Doukou, Suanziren, Binglang, Zhiqiao (stir-fried), Houpo (stir-fried with ginger), Banxia (prepared in decoction), Qiping (white part removed), and Juhong, and one qian of Dahuang with Nitre and roasted Licorice.
    Preparation: Prepare as one dose; use two zhongs of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and one red date, and boil until reduced to one zhong, taken before meals.

    Yizhong Wan - Strengthens the spleen and warms the stomach, aids in the digestion of cold phlegm. Treats fullness, bloating, acid regurgitation, intermittent pain in the heart and abdomen, and reluctance to eat.
    Ingredients: Two liang each of Shenchu (fried), Mianjie (fried), and Ganjiang (roasted), and two liang of Gao Liangjiang (fried), Chenpi, half a liang each of Zhiqiao (insides removed and stir-fried) and Nutmeg (wrapped in dough and cooked), and half a liang of Clove.
    Preparation: Grind to a fine powder, mix with dough to form pills the size of wutong seeds; each dose is fifty pills, taken before meals, with warm rice drink or plain soup.[61p]

    　　姜枣丸　治胃寒痰逆，噫气吞酸，胸膈不利，不思饮食。　　生姜去皮切片，焙干，四两　附子炮裂去皮脐　丁香各一两　　右为细末，用蒸熟枣肉和为丸如梧桐子大，每服十五丸，加至二十丸，不拘时候，米饮送下。

    Ginger Date Pills: Treats cold in the stomach with phlegm countercurrent, belching with sour taste, chest and diaphragm discomfort, and lack of appetite. Grind these into a fine powder, mix with steamed and mashed jujube flesh to form pills the size of a phoenix nut. Take fifteen pills, increasing to twenty, at any time, taken with rice drink.

    Qi Harmonizing Pills: Treats excessive belching due to Qi deficiency and turbidity rising.     Phlegm-Dispelling Fire Pills: Treats stomach fire with phlegm heat leading to belching. Equal parts of nux vomica, pinellia, cyperus, gypsum, and gardenia. Grind into powder, make pills soaked in ginger juice or take with ginger decoction.

    Ten Flavor Preserving Harmony Decoction: Treats stagnation from Qi deficiency in the stomach leading to belching. Combine with two cups of water, three slices of ginger, and two jujubes, simmer until reduced by a quarter, and take warm before meals.[62p]

    Zhiqiao Powder: Treats discomfort in the heart and chest, with frequent sighing and pain, gas akin to spoiled eggs. Ingredients: Zhiqiao, Bai Zhu, each five qian; Xiangfuzi, one liang; Binglang, two qian. Grind these into a fine powder. Take two qian each time, mixed with rice drink, three times a day, at any time.

    Bansheng Pill: Treats phlegm and fire resulting in belching. Ingredients: Banxia (ginger-prepared), Nanzheng (ginger-prepared), soft gypsum, Xiangfuzi, and Zhizi, each in equal parts. Grind into powder and form pills with Shenqu.

    Single Formulas:

    For chronic cough and belching: Half a cup of fresh ginger juice, one spoon of honey, decoct warm and sip; take three doses for recovery.

    For various belching: Two liang of tangerine peel, remove the pith, one sheng of water, decoct to five portions, take at once. Adding Zhiqiao is also good.

    For persistent belching: Four liang of Sichuan pepper, toasted and ground, form into pills the size of a walnut; take ten pills each time, wash down with vinegar soup for remarkable effect.

    For febrile belching: Half a liang of Zhiqiao, one qian of Mu Xiang, grind into powder; take one qian with plain water, don't know if to repeat.

    If belching prevents eating: Take cliff honey and hold it in your mouth, swallow gently.[63p]

    　　　　针灸

    　　《灵枢经》云：黄帝曰：人之噫者，何气使然？岐伯曰：寒气客于胃，厥逆从下上散，复出于胃，故为噫补足太阴阳明。一曰：补眉本也。　　《脉经》曰：右手关前寸口阴绝者，无肺脉也。苦短气咳逆，喉中塞，噫逆，刺手阳明经治阳。　　《甲乙经》曰：热病发热烦满而欲呕哕，三日以往，不得汗，怵惕胸胁痛，不可反侧，咳满溺赤，大便血，衄不止，呕吐血，气逆噫不止，嗌中痛，食不下，善渴，舌中烂，掌中热，饮呕，劳宫主之。　　肠中寒，胀满善噫，闻食臭，胃气不足，肠鸣腹痛泄，食不化，心下胀，三里主之。　　热病汗不出，善噫，腹胀满，胃热讝语，解溪主之。　　《千金方》曰：少海，主气逆噫哕呕。　　陷谷，主腹大满，喜噫。[64p]

    Oh, expel the sour gas: brew water from the red bean for a while, take one cup for effect.

    For those suffering from cold damage and experiencing intermittent belching day and night: take equal parts of prickly ash and galanga, grind into a powder, take two qian, with six sheng of water, boil ten times, add a little vinegar and take it.

    Acupuncture

    The "Spirit Pivot" states: The Yellow Emperor asked: What qi causes human belching? Qi Bo replied: Cold qi resides in the stomach, causing counterflow that disperses upward, thus belching is a supplement to the greater yin and yang brightness. It can also be said to nourish the root of the eyebrows. The "Pulse Classic" states: The right hand's front wrist position shows a lack of lung pulse. Bitter, shortness of breath, coughing upwards, throat obstruction, and reversed belching, need to puncture the yang brightness channel for treatment.

    The "Shell and Leaf Classic" states: In heat illness, if there is fever, anxiety, fullness, and a desire to vomit, and after three days no sweating occurs, with palpitations in the chest and flanks, cannot turn over, contented cough, red urination, bloody stools, continuous nosebleeds, vomiting blood, counterflow belching without ending, throat pain, loss of appetite, great thirst, tongue ulcers, palm heat, and vomiting after drinking, one should treat the labor palace.

    Cold within the intestines, feeling distended with a tendency to belch, smelling food odors, insufficient stomach qi, bowel sounds with abdominal pain and diarrhea, undigested food, fullness below the heart, treat the point three li.

    In heat illness when there is no sweating, prone to belching, abdominal fullness, and the stomach is hot and talking nonsense, treat the remedy stream point.

    The "Thousand Golden Prescriptions" states: The lesser sea point governs counterflow belching and vomiting. The trapped valley point governs large abdominal fullness with a tendency to belch.[64p]

    　　蠡沟，主数噫，恐悸，气不足，腹中悒悒。　　大敦，主哕噫。又灸巨阙。
    　　劳宫，主气逆噫不止。
    　　噫哕膈中气闭寒，灸腋下聚毛下附胁宛宛中，五十壮。　　噫哕呕逆，灸石关百壮。

    　　　　医案

    　　《丹溪心法》曰：宣州人病心下蓄积痞闷，或作痛，多噫败卵气，用枳壳散，证皆除。气上筑心膈，噫气稍宽，脉之右关弱短，左关左尺长洪大而数，此肝有热，宜泻肝补脾，用青皮一钱，白朮二钱半，木通、甘草各二钱，煎下保和丸十五粒、抑青丸二十粒而愈。
    [65p]

    Líquōu is associated with sighing; fear and anxiety arise, with insufficient qi and a feeling of distress in the abdomen. Dàdūn is related to belching and also involves moxibustion at Jùquè.

    Láogōng pertains to qi counterflow, causing persistent belching.

    When belching and hiccups arise due to a blockage and coldness in the diaphragm, moxibustion is applied to the area beneath the armpits and beside the ribs, applying fifty strong strokes. For belching, hiccups, and nausea, a hundred strong strokes of moxibustion are applied at Shígān.

    The "Ancient and Modern Medical Compendium" states: for belching, one should target the middle epigastric point of the spleen channel.

    Medical Case Study

    The "Dànxī Xīnfǎ" mentions a patient from Xuanzhou with accumulation and stagnation beneath the heart, causing pain and frequent belching of rotting gas. Using Zhǐkè powder, the symptoms were resolved. Qi accumulation in the heart and diaphragm led to slight easing of belching, while the right pulse was weak and short, and the left guān and left chǐ were long, strong, and rapid, indicating heat in the liver. This requires draining the liver and tonifying the spleen, using one qian of Qingpi, two and a half qian of Baizhu, and two qian each of Mutong and Gancao, decocted, then taking fifteen grains of Bǎohé pills and twenty grains of Yìqīng pills for recovery.[65p]
